Important News

Capital Holds Huanghuagang Memorial 37

Central Party Headquarters:

On the morning of the 29th, at 9 o'clock, the Central Party Headquarters held a memorial service for the martyrs of Huanghuagang. Those in attendance were Central Committee members Chiang Kai-shek, Kong Xiangxi, Shao Yuanchong, Zhou Qigang, Wang Chonghui, Chen Lifu, Ma Chaojun, Liu Luyin, Yu Jingtang, Kexinge, and others, as well as representatives from various organizations and Party staff, totaling over 600 people. Chairman Chiang Kai-shek presided, and Ma Chaojun gave a report. The details of the meeting are recorded below:

Venue Arrangement:

The main gate of the Central Party Headquarters was adorned with a cloth banner in black ink, with the couplet: "Commemorating the revolutionary martyrs who did not fear death." The couplet read: "The revolutionary martyrs were the pioneers who assisted Premier Sun in creating the Republic of China," "The revolutionary martyrs were the patriots who sacrificed themselves to realize the Three Principles of the People." The second gate was decorated with pine branches and also had a banner with a couplet. The banner read: "The spirit of the revolutionary martyrs is immortal." The couplet read: "Generous in eliminating enemies, with great benevolence and courage," "Calmly embracing death, unyielding and indomitable." The auditorium was adorned with a banner with a couplet. The banner read: "Complete the unfinished legacy of the revolutionary martyrs." The couplet read: "March 29th is a page in revolutionary history that shocked the world and moved the gods," "March 29th is the beginning of the Three Principles of the People illuminating the globe and shining for centuries." On the stage, the spirit tablets of the revolutionary martyrs were placed in the center, flanked by wreaths from the Central Executive Committee and the Central Supervisory Committee.

Opening Ceremony:

(1) All stand in solemn respect.

(2) Play mournful music.

(3) Sing the Party anthem.

(4) Bow three times to the Party and national flag, the portrait of Premier Sun Yat-sen, and the spirit tablets of the martyrs.

(5) The chairman respectfully reads Premier Sun's will.

(6) Three minutes of silence.

(7) Report.

(8) Play mournful music.

(9) Ceremony concludes.

Ma Chaojun's Report:

In brief, today is the memorial day of March 29th, which is the most glorious event in the revolutionary history of twenty years ago. Twenty years ago, our nation was a nation oppressed by both imperialism and the Manchu Qing Dynasty. Premier Sun, in order to seek national independence, called on comrades at home and abroad to create this revolutionary cause. Although the March 29th revolution failed, the nation was awakened and the world was shocked, hence the success of the Wuchang Uprising, which was the price paid by the March 29th martyrs. The process of the March 29th comrades sacrificing themselves for righteousness is now briefly recounted on this occasion. Before March 29th, Premier Sun failed in his efforts to mobilize the New Army and went overseas to raise funds, leaving Huang Xing, Zhao Boxian, Hu Hanmin, and others to guard the Hong Kong headquarters. The comrades all worked separately, with propaganda and mobilization being conducted in secret, and expenses being borne by the comrades themselves. By February, the situation became increasingly urgent, and Manchu officials in Guangzhou were arresting Party members everywhere. At that time, the comrades believed that if they did not launch an uprising quickly, the opportunity would be lost. They decided to launch the uprising on February 15th, but the mobilization of all parties was not yet complete, and the purchased firearms had not yet arrived, so they postponed it to March 15th. At that time, comrades from overseas also gathered one after another, but because the Hong Kong government and the Manchu officials in Guangzhou were heavily guarded, it was difficult to act quickly. It was postponed to March 25th when the place where the comrades in Guangzhou hid their military weapons was discovered by Manchu officials. As the opportunity became more urgent, Huang Xing decided in Guangzhou on the 28th that the next day (29th) at 3 pm, the comrades would carry pistols and bombs and advance towards various government offices, taking the blowing of the deer horn as a signal. Huang led a part of the troops to attack the governor's office. Naval Admiral Li Zhun sent Wen Dexiong to lead a battalion of soldiers to reinforce the governor's office. When they arrived at Shuangmend, they met Fang Shengdong. Wen had a relationship with our party, and he was asking Fang about the situation. Fang mistakenly thought that Wen was leading troops to attack, so he preemptively attacked and wiped out Wen. At that time, all four cities had revolutionary flags, and there was great chaos in the city, but the revolutionary army was ultimately outnumbered and failed to achieve a complete success. Huang was injured in the attack on the governor's office and fled from the East Gate, fortunately escaping. At 5 am the next morning, Zhao Boxian led several hundred reinforcements from Hong Kong by boat to the province. Knowing that the event had failed, he rushed to Henan and embraced Huang Xing and cried bitterly. In fact, more than just seventy-two people died in this uprising, but only seventy-two martyrs are known today. After the failure of the March 29th uprising, Manchu officials sent out detectives to search for revolutionary party members, and the comrades all knew that Guangzhou was prepared. Therefore, they changed their strategy and went to various provinces to mobilize, which led to the Wuchang Uprising and the national response, and the national revolution succeeded. Premier Sun said that if the revolution does not succeed, then we will die for the cause. Now that the revolutionary cause has not yet been fully completed, we should commemorate the martyrs by following Premier Sun's teachings, continuing the legacy of the martyrs, and working hard to build the nation. This is the meaning of commemorating the martyrs today.

After the report, mournful music was played and the ceremony concluded.

Capital Circles:

On the same morning, at 9 o'clock, various circles in the capital held a grand meeting to commemorate the revolutionary martyrs in the Nanjing City Party Headquarters Auditorium. Over a hundred people attended, including City Executive Committee members Xiao Jishan, Lai Lian, and representatives from various organizations and groups. Chairman Xiao Jishan gave a speech after the ceremony, briefly stating that before the Xinhai Revolution, China was subject to imperialist aggression from the outside and the autocratic rule of the Manchu Qing Dynasty from the inside. The revolutionary martyrs of our party deeply knew that revolution was necessary to save the country, so they spared no effort to promote revolution at the cost of everything. At that time, I do not know how many comrades sacrificed themselves, especially in the March 29th campaign. Their spirit of sacrificing themselves for righteousness was enough to sway the public opinion at that time. Therefore, not many months after the March 29th campaign, the Wuchang Uprising succeeded. Today, commemorating the martyrs should know that the sacrifices of the martyrs were entirely for the country and the nation. We should eliminate selfishness, learn from the spirit of sacrifice of the martyrs, work hard to overthrow imperialism, abolish unequal treaties, and seek national construction. Only in this way can commemoration be meaningful. Then Lai Lian gave a speech, briefly stating that the success of the Xinhai Revolution was entirely the result of the sacrifices of the martyrs. Today, commemorating the martyrs should be based on the spirit of sacrifice of the martyrs, work hard to complete the unfinished will of the martyrs, and eliminate corrupt and degenerate elements in order to be worthy of the martyrs. After the speech, slogans were shouted and the meeting was adjourned.

Panchen Lama's Representative Reports on Sino-Tibetan Relations 38

Losang Nangyal, the chief of staff of the Panchen Lama, and Senator Jin Xiaoben, representatives of the Panchen Lama, came to Beijing from Ujimqin Banner in Inner Mongolia to report on the Panchen Lama's plan to come to Beijing for an audience. They have already visited the Presidential Office and ministers of various Yuan and departments, submitting letters and completing negotiations. They are now waiting for the Panchen Lama's telegram to arrive in Shenyang, preparing to go to Shenyang to report on their visit to Beijing and then accompany the Panchen Lama south.

The representatives also hosted a reception for the press at Jinlingchun at noon on the 29th, attended by more than 50 people, and reported in detail on Sino-Tibetan relations. Their statement was as follows:

"Shun exiled the Sanmiao people to Sanwei. Sanwei is present-day Tibet. The so-called Tubo people are descendants of the Sanmiao. In the Zhou Dynasty, they were called the Western Rong. When King Ping moved east, they had contact with the Central Plains. In the Han Dynasty, they were called the Western Qiang. Emperor Wu ordered them to live in the borderlands. During the reign of Emperor Huai of Jin, they once lived in Chang'an. In the Kaihuang period of the Sui Dynasty, they destroyed the Shi Guhun, and the Tuoba clan began to establish their kingdom. In the Tang Dynasty, they were erroneously called Tubo. At that time, their Zanpu Songtsen Gampo was quite strong and repeatedly invaded the Tang border, seeking marriage with the Tang Dynasty. In the fifteenth year of Zhenguan, Princess Wencheng married Tibet. At that time, the Tang Emperor and the Tibetan Zanpu each led their ministers to slaughter livestock, inserted blood, and announced to the gods of heaven, earth, sun, moon, mountains, rivers, and the state, establishing a great alliance, carving stones and erecting monuments in the Grand Assembly Hall. The two countries will forever abide by their oaths, help each other, and fulfill the duties of nephews and uncles. In the first year of Jingyun, Emperor Ruizong again married Princess Jincheng to the Tibetan Zanpu. The escorts of the two princesses numbered tens of thousands, all marrying Tibetan women, and the friendship was extraordinary. During the Song Dynasty, they lived in peace. In the first year of Baoyou during the reign of Emperor Xianzong of the Yuan Dynasty, the Pacification Commissioner's Office and the Marshal's Office of the Six Pacification Commissioners of the Tubo were established in Hezhou. Emperor Shizu took Pagpa as his teacher and granted him the title of Grand Treasure Dharma King, ordering him to create the Mongolian script. In the sixth year of Zhiyuan, the Pacification Commissioner's Office of U-Tsang was re-established, dividing its territory into counties and ordering Pagpa to lead it. His disciples were mostly Situ, Sikong, and Dukes, all wearing gold and jade seals. This is the ancestor of the Red Sect. Emperor Taizu of the Ming Dynasty granted Namgyal Palzang of U-Tsang the title of Grand Master of the Flourishing Buddha Treasure Kingdom, in charge of the entire territory of U-Tsang. In the third year of Yongle, the title of Grand Treasure Dharma King and the Tathagata of Buddhist Exposition was granted to Khalima of U-Tsang. His disciples were granted the titles of Dharma Kings such as Mahayana and Mahakaruna, as well as Bodhisattvas who expounded, transformed, protected, and assisted in teaching and accumulated merit. In the tenth year of Yongle, the Grand Master of the Western Sky Buddha and nine to eighteen Grand Masters were also granted.

In the fifteenth year of Yongle, Tsongkhapa was born in Xining, Qinghai. He initially studied the Red Sect, but later made major reforms and became the ancestor of the Yellow Sect. He ordered his two great disciples, the Dalai Lama and the Panchen Lama, to reincarnate in each generation to govern religion. In the early Qing Dynasty, in the seventh year of Chongde, the Panchen Lama sent representatives to Shengjing to offer local products. Emperor Taizong treated them generously, granting them the title of Vajra Master and decreeing that the Panchen Lama and the Dalai Lama, when young, should follow the military and when older, should study the classics, treating them with the etiquette of a teacher. Before long, the power of Tsangpa Gyawe became strong, unifying the front and back of Tibet, worshiping the Red Sect Lama Taranatha, and suppressing the Yellow Sect's Fourth Dalai Lama, Yonten Gyatso, and prohibiting its re-establishment. At that time, Gushri Khan of Qinghai, who believed in the Yellow Sect, heard of the unrest in Tibet and sent people to Tibet to investigate, encountering the Fourth Panchen Lama, Lobsang Chökyi Gyaltsen, who knew of the imminent demise of the Yellow Sect. Gushri Khan then ordered Güshi Tenzin Chögyal to lead 3,000 soldiers into Tibet to join the Panchen Lama to quell the Tibetan rebellion and re-establish the Fifth Dalai Lama, Lobsang Gyatso. Gushri Khan reported the facts of pacifying Tibet to the Qing court. Emperor Shizu sent officials to urge the Panchen Lama to come, but the Panchen Lama, being nearly a hundred years old, was inconvenient to travel far, claiming that he and the Dalai Lama were equal in character and learning, despite their age difference. He instructed the Dalai Lama to come to the mainland immediately. Therefore, the Dalai Lama traveled to Beijing, China in the ninth year of Shunzhi. In the fifty-fifth year of Kangxi, China pacified the Zunghar invasion of Tibet and erected a monument in the Grand Assembly Hall. In the seventh year of Yongzheng, China pacified the rebellion of Tibetan minister Arbu-Ba, punishing the chief culprits after investigating. Lang-A was initially left to serve as the vice resident minister, leading 2,000 soldiers from Sichuan and Shaanxi to be stationed in the front and back of Tibet to protect the religion. In the fifteenth year of Qianlong, China executed Polo-Nai County King Zhulmo Tedan for disturbing Tibet, robbing and killing the resident commander Fu Qing and others, knowing that Tibet's politics and religion could not be separated. It was then stipulated that the Tibetan king would be selected from among the Panchen Lama, the Dalai Lama, and the four great Hutuktu, and traditional inheritance was not allowed. Another 1,500 soldiers were added to guard Tibet. Twenty years later, China pacified Yili for Tibet, allowing Tibet to be forever free from the Zunghar threat. Forty-five years later, the Sixth Panchen Lama came to China to celebrate Emperor Gaozong's birthday, passing away due to smallpox at the Yellow Temple. Fifty-seven years later, the Gurkha forcefully invaded Tibet, occupying the western territory. China sent Fukangan and Hailancha to lead troops to recapture the lost territory of Tibet. The troops arrived at the Gurkha capital, and the Gurkhas, in fear, surrendered, stipulating a tribute every five years. From then on, Fukangan, under the command of the Qing court, together with the Sichuan governor and the Panchen Lama and the Dalai Lama, stipulated the etiquette for the resident ministers, treating them equally with the Dalai Lama and the Panchen Lama, and determining the official system and tribute system for the front and back of Tibet, as well as all tax matters, and comprehensively planning national defense and military system, as well as protecting the indigenous military quotas in the front and back of Tibet. All military expenses were paid by the national treasury. Sichuan paid an annual subsidy of more than one hundred thousand taels of silver, which was part of the expenses for the resident officials and soldiers in Tibet. Political power belonged to the Tibetan king, and religious power belonged to the Dalai Lama and the Panchen Lama. The front and back of Tibet did not govern each other, each governing itself. All matters were directly discussed with the resident ministers. Military and diplomatic affairs were discussed by the Dalai Lama, the Panchen Lama, the three major monasteries, and the resident ministers. When necessary, instructions were sought from the Chinese government. The above-mentioned friendly relations between China and Tibet can be imagined. Therefore, the Tibetan people, all those over the age of thirty, still look east, hoping to restore the old friendship between China and Tibet. Throughout the generations, the Dalai Lama and the Panchen Lama have assisted each other and have had no problems. The front and back of Tibet are like one family, without dividing borders. Unexpectedly, since the second year of the Republic of China, communication between China and Tibet has been interrupted, and the feelings of both sides cannot be expressed. The Panchen Lama believes that Tibet has been repeatedly oppressed by strong neighbors for hundreds of years, and has been protected from destruction by China's strength. As for the salaries and food for the soldiers stationed in Tibet, as well as various items for almsgiving, China has spent millions of taels of silver annually. Even during the British invasion of Tibet in the twenty-ninth year of Guangxu, China paid the war expenses. Without boasting or seeking favors, recalling the past and thinking about the present, the good relationship is still vivid. Not forgetting China's actual benefits, in the winter of the twelfth year, he came to the mainland in person, not afraid of the difficulties and obstacles, to express his unwavering loyalty. At that time, the military was restless, and there was no way to appeal. He traveled extensively through the provinces of Zhili, Fengtian, Shanxi, Shandong, Jiangsu, and Zhejiang, as well as various leagues and banners in Inner Mongolia, chanting scriptures and expounding religions. Time passed quickly. Now, the revolution has succeeded, the north and south are unified, and the national government has no worries at home and can plan to consolidate the borders of the entire nation. The joy can be imagined. It is also heard that envoys between China and Tibet are traveling back and forth, and Tibet has sent plenipotentiary representatives to Beijing to participate in the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission, and is preparing to participate in the National Tibetan Conference. This is even more gratifying. Therefore, it is planned to come to the capital in the shortest possible time to listen to the good news between China and Tibet, hoping that the national territory will be as solid as a rock and that the happiness of the Tibetan people will be increased and the relationship between China and Tibet will be restored. Therefore, these unworthy ones are sent to Beijing in advance to negotiate everything, and now these unworthy ones have obtained the consent of the comrades of the national government to report to Shenyang soon, hoping that the Panchen Buddha will come soon and peacefully resolve the Tibetan affairs to fulfill his original intention of coming east."

Qingdao Native Product Merchants Still on Strike 39

Party and Government Authorities Have Telegraphed the Central Government

Qingdao Correspondence:

The strike by Qingdao native product merchants has lasted for ten days without resolution. Laborers are unemployed, and commerce is stagnant, which is detrimental to the local community. The local Party and government authorities have tried to mediate, but the Inspection Bureau, due to its vested interests, refuses to abolish the inspection fees, leading to a stalemate. In view of this, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday submitted a petition to the Municipal Steering Committee, requesting that it telegraph to the Central Government for permission to waive inspection fees to maintain the market and alleviate the merchants' difficulties. The Municipal Steering Committee, upon receiving the petition, forwarded it to the Central Government yesterday for review and approval. The telegram reads as follows:

"To the esteemed Central Executive Committee in Nanjing,

Qingdao native product merchants have repeatedly appealed to the Commodity Inspection Bureau regarding the inspection fees for peanuts and peanut oil sold domestically, but their appeals have not been approved. As a result, they have stopped trading, and the situation is urgent. Inspection of goods not intended for export is unnecessary and harmful to the people's livelihood. We earnestly request that your committee instruct the National Government to order the Ministry of Industry to allow exemptions from inspection fees to alleviate the merchants' difficulties. We await your response with utmost anticipation."

At the same time, the Municipal Government, based on the request of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, also telegraphed the Ministry of Industry today, requesting leniency for the merchants' difficulties and exemption from inspection fees. It also sent a letter to the Commodity Inspection Bureau, temporarily waiving inspection fees and awaiting resolution from the Ministry of Industry. The telegram to the Ministry of Industry is recorded below:

"To the esteemed Ministry of Industry in Nanjing,

According to the Qingdao Municipal Chamber of Commerce's forwarding of the petition from the Guild of Stacks and Native Product Merchants, the merchants have requested exemption from inspection fees for native products sold domestically. Previously, the Ministry approved that all non-export goods, except for cotton and goods specifically approved by the Ministry, would be exempt from inspection fees, and the Inspection Bureau announced its implementation. Subsequently, the Bureau informed them that, according to the Ministry's telegram, peanuts and peanut oil, whether exported or sold domestically, would still be subject to inspection fees. Due to the conflicting instructions, the merchants are at a loss. Although they have telegraphed the Ministry to request the revocation of the order, the Bureau has decided to resume levying fees on March 16th. The merchants' business is difficult, and they have reluctantly stopped trading on the 17th, hoping to receive leniency. The merchants believe that raw rice and oil are related to the people's food, and inspection is cumbersome, and fees increase the price of food. Tianjin, Hankou, Shanghai, Guangzhou, and other places do not levy inspection fees, so Qingdao cannot be an exception. We earnestly request that you telegraph to the Central Government for permission to waive inspection fees to alleviate the merchants' difficulties. Please reply." (26th)

Important News 2

Shandong Salt Merchants in Great Panic 41

Affected by New Policies

Jinan Correspondence:

The new salt law has been passed by the Legislative Yuan for many years, and the abolishment of the salt concession system is imminent. Shandong Province, being a salt-producing region, has caused great panic among salt merchants. According to a certain salt merchant, after the Legislative Yuan decided on the new salt law, Commissioner Zhang Yun tried his best to reassure the salt merchants, saying that the implementation procedures of the new salt law were still many, and that it would not be implemented until two years later at the earliest. Everyone should not panic. But in fact, it has been greatly affected, even if they do not want to panic, they cannot. One reason is that the salt merchants rely entirely on selling salt, but recently a slogan has appeared in various counties - "Quickly eat cheap salt" - and it is everywhere. As a result, buyers are unwilling to buy in bulk, and sales have plummeted. Second, the salt merchants' business has been declining in recent years, relying entirely on borrowing money from banks. Now that it is time to sell ya salt (used for pickling toon) and sell jian salt (for pickling silkworm cocoons), the new salt law has suddenly been announced, and bankers are unwilling to lend money. Salt merchants are almost unable to transport salt. With these two major reasons, how can they not panic? Currently, salt merchants in this province plan to state their difficulties to the Central Government and request a postponement of the implementation of the new salt law to alleviate the merchants' difficulties.

According to reports, the current annual sales of salt in this province is less than 300 permits (each permit transports 500 bags of salt, each bag weighing 100 catties). In the 13th year of the Republic of China, annual sales could reach 700 permits, more than double that amount. The biggest reason for this is that years of war have led to a proliferation of smuggled salt (soldiers transporting salt). Salt in the Jiaodong counties is sufficient for ten years, all of which was hoarded in previous years smuggled salt. In the thirteenth year, the number of salt merchants (those with permits) and traveling merchants (those who rent permits to transport salt) in this province was no less than 600 or 700. Because Zhang Zongchang handled salt permit registration, traveling merchants advanced the registration fees of more than 3 million for the salt merchants. Salt merchants, due to years of war and the disruption of salt sales, and the inability to rent out their permits, have had bankruptcies reaching more than 200. They could not repay the loans of the traveling merchants. The traveling merchants, due to the lack of salt sales and the bankruptcies of the salt merchants, have also had bankruptcies reaching more than 200. To this day, there are only about 100 salt merchants and traveling merchants. The three most famous companies, Dingli, have closed down. Dingxin has been affected by the Tengyi banditry, and its business is sluggish. Dingyu is better. The salt tax in this province (more than 7 million yuan annually in the 13th year, and never more than 3 million yuan since then) has slightly improved since the end of the war last year, but it will soon be affected by the new salt law. In the future, the implementation of the new salt law will directly and indirectly lead to the unemployment of no less than 200,000 people in the salt merchant community in this province.

Shandong Business Tax Set to Begin Next Month 42

The Province is Divided into Thirteen Tax Collection Zones

Jinan Correspondence: Since the abolition of Likin taxes on January 1st, the province has established a Business Tax Preparatory Committee to handle preparations. The committee dispatched numerous members to conduct surveys in various zones. Originally, it was planned that the surveys would be completed this month, and tax collection would begin on April 1st. However, due to the fact that the investigators still have over ten areas that have not yet been investigated and the urgency to begin collection, the Bureau held its tenth regular meeting yesterday and resolved to request the provincial government to extend the committee's term by one month, and to announce the commencement of tax collection from April 1st. Areas that have not been surveyed will be re-surveyed concurrently. After the regulations and detailed rules are approved by the Ministry of Finance, business licenses will be issued and taxes will be collected to avoid delays. The tax collection zones have been determined according to the current tobacco and alcohol tax zones, dividing the province into thirteen zones: 1. Jinan, 2. Tai'an, 3. Tengxian, 4. Jining, 5. Dong'e, 6. Linqing, 7. Jiyang, 8. Huimin, 9. Zhoucun, 10. Yizhou, 11. Weixian, 12. Jiaozhou, and 13. Yantai. Depending on the complexity of tax affairs in each zone, several tax collection offices will be established. It is estimated that the total annual revenue will not exceed two million yuan, which is insufficient to offset the monthly assistance provided by the central government after the abolition of Likin. The Bureau is currently planning to divide two or three additional zones outside of the existing thirteen, but such measures would only increase expenses, and the revenue may not increase significantly. The biggest reason is that the consolidated tax on goods in Qingdao has historically been a source of over one million yuan in annual revenue for the provincial government. Now that the business tax is allocated to the Qingdao municipal government, the provincial treasury has lost this significant income, which has a huge impact. Attached are the draft regulations for the collection of business tax in Shandong Province and the tax standards:

Regulations for the Collection of Business Tax in Shandong Province: (1) These regulations are based on the national general outline for the collection of business tax in various provinces and supplementary measures promulgated by the central government. (2) All businesses operating within the province, regardless of whether they are Chinese or foreign, shall comply with the provisions of these regulations to pay business tax, unless otherwise stipulated by law. (3) The collection of business tax shall be handled by bureaus established by the Finance Department based on the commercial prosperity of various localities. The location of the bureaus, organizational regulations, and expense budgets shall be determined separately. (4) The standards for collecting business tax are temporarily set as two types: (A) based on business turnover; (B) based on capital. (5) The tax rates for collecting business tax are stipulated as follows: (A) For those based on business turnover, the tax rate is divided into five levels: Level 1 is set at one per thousand, Level 2 at two per thousand, Level 3 at five per thousand, Level 4 at ten per thousand, and Level 5 at fifteen per thousand. (B) For those based on capital, the tax rate is divided into two levels: Level 1 is set at ten per thousand, and Level 2 at twenty per thousand. The tax standards and tax rate levels for each industry are specified separately in a table according to the type and nature of the business. (6) For businesses that should be taxed but are not listed in the tax table, the collection agency shall propose a tax rate based on the type and nature of the business and submit it to the Finance Department for approval. (7) Businesses that meet any of the following conditions are exempt from business tax: (A) Businesses with capital less than 500 yuan; (B) Enterprises operated by the state or local governments; (C) Those not for profit-making purposes. (8) All businesses that should be taxed, whether newly opened or previously established, must apply for a business license by providing the following information: (A) The type and name of the business and its location; (B) The name and origin of the business owner and their address; (C) The amount of business capital; (D) The estimated annual business income. The aforementioned business license must be renewed annually without any fee. (9) Business tax shall be collected once a month, and the Finance Department shall issue a unified tax receipt. (10) The calculation of business capital shall include all basic capital, reserve capital, public accumulation, and other funds actually available for business use. (11) If a business engages in multiple types of business with different tax rates, the tax amount shall be calculated separately for each type and then totaled for payment. (12) If a business has branches within the province, the business tax may be paid by the head office. If the head office or a branch is located outside the province, the business tax shall be paid only for the branches or head office located within the province. (13) For businesses engaged in the sale of goods, those that specialize in wholesale may be taxed at half the established rate. The same applies to those engaged in partial wholesale. (14) If a manufacturing business directly retails its manufactured goods, the retail portion shall still be taxed according to the tax rate stipulated for the sale of goods. (15) Businesses that are taxed based on business turnover shall calculate their business turnover once every year in June and at the end of December and report it to the relevant collection agency before the 15th of the following month. However, if the business ceases operation in less than half a year, it shall be reported at the time of cessation. (16) If a business undergoes changes in its operations, adds new capital, reorganizes, changes its registration, or relocates, it shall immediately report to the relevant collection agency and surrender the old license for a new one. (17) When a business ceases operations, it must report to the relevant collection agency within fifteen days, along with the business license, and pay all outstanding taxes due before the cessation of operations. (18) If a business license is lost or damaged, a new license shall be issued upon payment of a license fee of one yuan. (19) Businesses with capital less than 500 yuan and branches opened within the province whose business tax has already been paid by the head office may be issued a supplementary business license by the Finance Department to indicate the distinction. The aforementioned supplementary business license must be renewed annually, and a fee of five jiao shall be charged. (20) After the establishment of business tax bureaus in each county, a business tax review committee shall be established in each bureau, and a business tax examination committee shall be established within the Finance Department. The organization and review rules of each committee shall be determined separately. (21) The collection agencies shall announce the collected business tax amounts monthly and compile an annual collection record, which shall be reviewed by the business tax review committee. After all members have signed it, it shall be submitted to the Finance Department for approval and promulgation. (22) The collection agency may, when necessary, inspect the business owner's books, documents, goods, and other items. (23) Business owners who refuse inspection, report more than is accurate, conceal information, operate without a license, or delay in paying taxes shall be subject to supplementary taxes and required to obtain a license, and shall also be subject to penalties, the rules for which shall be determined separately. (24) Tax collection personnel in each bureau who overcharge, extort, collude with merchants to conceal and evade taxes, or engage in other illegal activities shall be punished according to the severity of the circumstances. (25) All tax and penalty revenues collected by each bureau shall be reported and submitted to the treasury of the Finance Department within the prescribed time limit. The rules for such remittances shall be determined separately. (26) Each bureau shall prepare monthly and annual report forms for all taxes and penalties collected and submit them for special review. The format of the forms shall be determined separately. (27) Two percent of the tax revenue collected by each bureau shall be set aside as printing expenses for the printing of tax certificates and receipts. (28) After the implementation of the business tax, all existing tooth taxes, pawn taxes, slaughter taxes, and other taxes and levies in the province that are similar to the business tax shall be converted into business tax and collected at the original tax rates. (29) Detailed implementation rules for these regulations shall be determined separately. (30) These regulations shall be promulgated and implemented after being resolved by the Provincial Government Council and reported to the Ministry of Finance for record. Any matters not covered may be submitted for amendment at any time.

Shandong Province Business Tax Rate Standards: Manufacturing, printing and publishing, transportation, contracting, and trust industries: tax rate of two per thousand based on business turnover. Transportation industry: tax rate of five per thousand based on business turnover. Rental of goods, storage yards, barber shops, and bathhouses: tax rate of ten per thousand based on business turnover. Photography studios, hotels and restaurants, and entertainment venues: tax rate of fifteen per thousand based on business turnover. Sale of goods: tax rate of one per thousand to fifteen per thousand based on business turnover. Savings societies: Type A without prizes, tax rate of ten per thousand based on capital. Type B with prizes, tax rate of twenty per thousand based on capital. Insurance, stock exchange, and money exchange industries: tax rate of twenty per thousand based on capital. (Types and Tax Rates for Sale of Goods) Category 1: Grain, firewood, coal, salt, cloth, soy sauce shops, brick, tile, lime and stone industries, and tailoring: tax rate of one per thousand. Category 2: Cotton, cotton weaving, hemp weaving, traditional Chinese medicine, fan, straw weaving, pastry, packaging carton, rubbing, bamboo, wood and rattan, shoes and hats, paper, writing brush and ink, used clothing, ironware, umbrella and mat, domestic suitcase, coarse ceramics, yarn, Southern paper, thread, ribbon and towel, silk and satin, books and stationery: tax rate of two per thousand. Category 3: Tea, eggs, pigment, candle soap, silk cocoons, cured meat and ham, matches, groceries, fine porcelain and glassware, lace, embroidery, hairnet, copper and tinware, fruit, livestock and fresh fish: tax rate of five per thousand. Category 4: Sugar, leather, hardware, electrical appliances, fur, copper and iron bed, and imported general merchandise: tax rate of ten per thousand. Category 5: Rubber, felt, Western clothing, imported paper, wool and foreign cloth, Western medicine, tea and canned food, Western furniture, ginseng, bird's nest and seafood, antiques, jewelry, gold, silver and pearls, clocks and watches, cosmetics and art supplies, phonographs, soda and iced food, dental inlay, incense, candles and paper foil: tax rate of fifteen per thousand.

Truth About the Incident on Nanri Island, Fujian 43

Reasons for Island Residents' Attack on the Island Affairs Bureau

Fuzhou Correspondence: An incident occurred on Nanri Island recently in which island residents attacked the Island Affairs Bureau. An investigation reveals that the root cause of the incident was that some unscrupulous individuals opened gambling dens during the Lantern Festival celebrations held by the island residents a month ago. Many bandits from nearby areas also infiltrated, and the Island Affairs Bureau, being far away, was unaware of this. A certain island resident, Mr. Jia, suffered repeated losses in gambling and ran out of money. He asked his landlord for a loan, but the landlord refused, which made him very unhappy. He went to the bureau and reported to the Bureau Chief, Qiu Zhenjie. Upon hearing this, Qiu sent many police officers to arrest the bandits on the fourteenth. The bandits scattered upon hearing the news, but one or two residents of the island were unable to escape and hid under a bed. The police officers mistakenly thought they were bandits and opened fire, killing one person. This incited public outrage. The police officers had not been gone for an hour when the island residents, armed with weapons, surrounded the bureau. As a result, the police officers were outnumbered, and a total of 59 officers and police were killed. It is said that 26 of them were brought by Qiu Zhenjie from Putian to the island to guard against pirates. Unexpectedly, they died at the hands of the island residents just a few days after arriving at the bureau. Qiu had only been in office for 40 days. Qiu also served concurrently as the head of the water police outpost. The family members of the personnel involved in this riot were also not spared, which is truly tragic. Wu Shu, the Director of the Maritime Public Security Bureau, immediately sent personnel to the island to investigate the truth. He also submitted a request to the provincial government yesterday to grant generous compensation to comfort the departed souls. (26th)

Shanxi Currency Plummets Amid Panic 44

Public Panic, Financial Disorder

Officials Hold Emergency Meeting

Relief Measures to Be Announced

Taiyuan Correspondence: The Shanxi currency (Jin鈔) plummeted in price the previous two days was already very unsettling. However, yesterday, the situation worsened. The rate of exchange rose to three yuan or more for one silver dollar, and it was difficult to purchase dollars at even that rate. The provincial bank, in order to maintain stability, sold 120,000 silver dollars, hoping to adjust the market. However, this had no practical effect. Since yesterday, the market has been in a state of extreme panic. Various businesses have been converting all their transactions to silver dollars. The teachers and staff of primary and secondary schools even held an emergency meeting at the Education Association this morning, seeking a solution. Seeing this situation, Shang Zhen was very concerned. The night before last, he held an emergency meeting at his private residence, inviting the Director of Finance, Fen Yantian, and the Assistant Manager of the Provincial Bank, Yan Zixiu. Although the outcome of the meeting is unknown, a certain member of the Provincial Committee stated that Shang was extremely angry at the merchants who were manipulating the financial situation. He was determined to severely punish them. The Finance Department had a carefully planned method to stabilize the currency, the general outline of which would be announced in the next day or two. A number of major merchants will be arrested. According to a prominent member of the business community, the Shanxi currency's continued plunge has caused extreme panic in society. Their only hope lies in whether the authorities have concrete measures. For the past few days, while the Shanxi currency has been plummeting, the authorities have been eager to provide relief, but they have not yet issued a plan to correct the situation. As a result, the general public has gone from hope to disappointment, from disappointment to panic, and from panic to the feeling that the Shanxi currency is about to become worthless. That is why the price of the currency has plummeted so drastically in the past few days. The current financial situation in this province is indeed at a dangerous point. Today, the only hope for a turnaround is if the government can provide thorough relief and establish a remedy as soon as possible. Such a situation cannot be remedied by severely punishing merchants who manipulate the market or holding lotteries to redeem currency. Furthermore, two issues are closely related to the rectification of the Shanxi currency: one is the issue of restoring and rectifying Shanxi financial bonds, and the other is the issue of investigating Yan Xishan's withdrawals when he left. Although the people of Shanxi have fervently requested the bond issue to be addressed, the government has yet to issue clear regulations, so the matter has been shelved for a long time. Yesterday, a certain official here received a private telegram from Beijing stating that the National Government authorities have discussed the Shanxi financial bond case several times. The central government has received over two hundred letters and telegrams from Shanxi people's organizations and the provincial government requesting the restoration of the 24 million financial bonds. Minister Song Ziwen has visited the Chairman to discuss this matter, who immediately decided to approve the request of the people of Shanxi and restore the bonds. It is expected to be submitted to the State Council meeting this week. This is good news. Regarding the investigation of Yan Xishan's withdrawals, it has been approved by the provincial government to form a joint investigation committee with representatives from the provincial government, the military, and the Chamber of Commerce. The committee will first conduct an investigation and then determine the course of action. The committee is scheduled to meet this morning at the General Chamber of Commerce. The degree to which the resolution of the Shanxi currency problem is connected to the progress of the above two matters can be asserted. The Shanxi currency is currently in a difficult situation, with the hardship of being difficult to both save and abandon. The impact on finance is small, but the direct impact on society and people's livelihoods is great. The meeting and discussion of the education community today is the beginning of this impact. (March 25th)

Disaster Situation in Huixian and Yanjin, Henan Province 45

Kaifeng Correspondence: Huixian is a small and poor county. In the past, Yan Xishan and Feng Yuxiang repeatedly levied money and grain and conscripted laborers and vehicles from the county. After Political Inspector Wang Boying investigated, the amount of money extorted from the county by Yan and Feng reached 200,000 yuan. Liu Chunrong's troops mutinied in the county and plundered at will, leaving no village spared within a hundred li around the city. The total loss exceeded 300,000 yuan. Recent investigations by Disaster Relief Committee members Li Chengyi and County Magistrate Su Zhongbin revealed the following: (1) Over 300 houses were burned; (2) 400 vehicles and over 1,400 mules and horses were requisitioned; (3) Property loss amounted to approximately 5 million yuan; (4) Wheat and flour worth over 104,000 yuan; (5) Straw and firewood worth over 8,900 yuan; (6) The average harvest for both the summer and autumn seasons was less than 40%. Currently, there are 30,000 poor households and 8,000 extremely poor households, all suffering from hunger and cold, with scenes of devastation everywhere. The tragic situation in the county can be seen in its entirety.

Yanjin is located in a strategic area between Kaifeng and Weihui, with mostly sandy soil and few houses for storage. The people's livelihood is extremely difficult. Last year, drought caused a sharp decline in the harvest of summer wheat. In the summer, floods caused water levels to rise to over a foot in flat areas. Subsequently, locusts appeared along the old course of the Yellow River, and the northeast of the county seat experienced heavy rain and hail. The autumn harvest was non-existent. The devastation caused by natural disasters was already unbearable, but military disasters occurred repeatedly, with endless supplies. According to the report submitted by the County Magistrate Peng Tingxuan and forwarded by the Provincial Government, Shi You'san's army occupied the area for over eight months, demanding silver and conscripting horses, vehicles, military wheat, and laborers, totaling 179,182 yuan. The Second Route Army exchanged banknotes for opium, and requisitions of vehicles and horses amounted to 22,089 yuan. The Sixth Route requisitioned vehicles and horses for 5,420 yuan. When Han Fuju was Chairman, 1,880 vehicles and horses were requisitioned, worth over 1,880 yuan. The Twenty-sixth Route requisitioned wheat worth 2,596 yuan. The Second Cavalry Division extorted 8,400 yuan, and the First Cavalry Division took mules and horses worth 240 yuan. Chen Tiao's army extorted money and requisitioned vehicles and horses for 12,826 yuan. In addition, the various armies that passed through requisitioned food, dug trenches, and conscripted laborers for 7,086 yuan. Such a small county suffered such losses that over 1,250 disaster victims fled. Currently, there are 12,320 extremely poor households and 41,170 poor households. The cries for help are unbearable to hear.

Zhao Chengshou Accompanies Him

The current Shanxi army has over 100,000 men, and it has been decided to pay only half of them. The generals will come to Shenyang one after another to discuss how to raise the remaining half. Inspector Fu Dianwei will come to Shenyang with Sun Dianying to report after completing the inspection with the central government inspectors in the next few days. I will end my mission after meeting with Deputy Commander Zhang. Zhao Chengshou stated that his unit originally had four cavalry divisions with over 10,000 men. After this disbandment, three brigades with six regiments, including over 7,000 officers and soldiers and over 7,000 horses, have been retained. Ji has completed the inspection. They are stationed in the Datong and Suiyuan areas. The total cost of salary and supplies is 200,000 yuan. At present, there is no source of funding, and the supply of provisions is very difficult. The disbanded soldiers have been given separation pay, and the remaining horses have been distributed to various infantry units. The Shanxi army has received considerable training and education. After this disbandment and reorganization, they can become a strong force for national defense. Zhao will visit Zhang on the 25th and stay in Shenyang for about ten days. (March 25th)

Formal Election of the Liaoning General Chamber of Commerce 49

Fifteen Executive Committee Members and Seven Supervisory Committee Members Elected

Shenyang Correspondence: The Liaoning General Chamber of Commerce held an election for the executive and supervisory committee members on the 24th. The meeting formally started at 9:00 AM. Zhao Jun, the Provincial Government Supervisor, and Li Kaijia, the Agricultural and Mining Department Supervisor, attended. Jin Enqi, the Chairman of the Preparatory Committee, Lu Guangji, the Head of the Labor Union, and over two hundred chairmen of various associations greeted the attendees. First, Chairman Jin Enqi gave an opening speech, stating that the Liaoning General Chamber of Commerce was ordered by the central government to hold elections today. It is an honor to have provincial government officials, officials from the Department of Agriculture and Mining, and reporters present to oversee the elections. According to the investigation, there are over 10,000 shops in the provincial capital, Dadong District, the Shenhai Road area, and the commercial port area. There are 56 members in the commercial associations and 10 members in the shops. Over 920 people are eligible to vote and be elected, which is several times more than even the most prosperous Shanghai. Therefore, we must pay serious attention to this election. I hope that everyone will act according to the law in this election to avoid any future embarrassment and to ensure the smooth development of the Chamber of Commerce. Provincial Government Supervisor Zhao Jun and Agricultural Department Supervisor Li Kaijia gave speeches, stating that the elected individuals should have expertise in economics or experience in commerce and should work for the benefit of the province's chamber of commerce and strive for the glory of the national business community. At a time when economic rights are being lost to foreign countries and the financial situation is declining, we should try to recover the lost rights and revitalize the endangered situation. Voting began at 11:00 AM and continued until 4:00 PM. Under the supervision of officials from the Provincial Government and the Department of Agriculture and Mining, the ballot boxes were opened and the votes were counted. As a result, fifteen executive committee members and seven supervisory committee members were elected. The list of executive committee members is as follows: Jin Enqi, Lu Guangji, Li Futang, Wang Tongxuan, Wang Xiaowei, Qi Zirong, Fang Xudong, Qiao Jinqing, Liu Guanyi, Gao Zhenduo, Wang Heng'an, Li Yunshan, Wang Minqing, Gong Tianmin, Liu Zhaoxiang. The association also decided to elect five standing committee members from the fifteen executive committee members at 2:00 PM on the 25th at the Chamber of Commerce. The entire executive committee will then elect one chairman from the five standing committee members to complete the reorganization. (March 25th)

Anhui Merchants Demand Abolition of Inland Customs Stations 50

Wuhu Correspondence: At the National Likin Abolition Conference, it was resolved that inland customs stations are through-taxes that must be abolished for the complete elimination of Likin. Therefore, it was resolved that customs stations outside fifty li should be abolished, and one month later, all customs stations within fifty li should be abolished. Recently, merchants in various regions have been calling for this, but the Ministry of Finance has replied that a comprehensive plan must be drawn up before a decision can be made on the abolition date, delaying it until now. The Anhui Provincial Federation of Commerce and the Wuhu County Chamber of Commerce believe that the abolition of customs stations has been overdue for a long time, and the business tax in the province has already been implemented, so the burden on merchants has actually increased. Furthermore, Wuhu is surrounded by customs stations, and merchants feel the pain deeply. In addition to submitting a request to the central government, they have also sent letters to various industry associations, asking them to unanimously advocate for the previous proposal to the central government. (28th)

Wuxi 52

Robbery and Injury Occur in Yangming Township: In the Sixth-Ninth Map of the Third District (Yangming Township), Zhang Zunsan, a resident of the Zhang Xiaomu Bridge area in the West Lane, currently operates the Hengchun Rice Store under the Kuatang Bridge outside the South Gate. At approximately 12:00 AM the night before last, more than ten robbers suddenly arrived, speaking in a strong Northern accent and carrying flashlights, knives, clubs, and homemade bombs. They broke open the front door and entered. Mr. Zhang and his wife were already asleep. After entering the room, the robbers went straight to the upstairs bedroom and dragged Mr. and Mrs. Zunsan out of bed. They tied them up with ropes and forced them to reveal where the silver was hidden. When Mr. and Mrs. Zhang were slow to answer, they were kicked violently by the robbers, causing serious injuries to their waists and other parts of their bodies. The robbers then burned the lower parts of Mr. and Mrs. Zunsan's bodies with candles and straw. Afterwards, they divided up to search for loot and left with the stolen goods, shouting loudly. After investigation, it was found that gold, silver jewelry, clothing, and other items worth approximately two hundred silver dollars had been stolen. The heads of the Third and Eighth Sub-bureaus of Public Security were informed and immediately led police to search for the robbers, but they had already fled far away and could not be apprehended. At the same time, more than twenty robbers also entered the home of Zhang Songnan, a resident of Xiaozhang Lane in the same district, and carried out a robbery, causing significant losses.

County Government Convenes a Meeting with Industrial and Commercial Groups: County Magistrate Pan of the County Government attaches great importance to the preparations for the election of People's Assembly representatives. Therefore, he convened a meeting with various industrial and commercial groups at 2:00 PM yesterday to discuss the matter. The following resolutions were made: 1. How should the election of industrial and commercial groups be divided into districts? Resolution: The polling station for industrial groups will be located at the Chamber of Commerce. The polling stations for worker groups will be located in four locations: East, South, West, and North. The East District will be located at the Silk Factory Workers' Union, the South District at the Zhang Wang Temple, the West District at the County Party Headquarters, and the North District at the Machine Furnace Factory Siping Engineers' Union. 1. Given the large number of voters in this election, in addition to managers and supervisors, how should additional assistants be added to each polling station? Resolution: Add sixteen people to each station. 1. How should the location for counting ballots be determined for each polling station? Resolution: Ballots will be counted at each polling station. 1. Should workers in various factories be given time off to participate in the election? Resolution: Workers should be given time off for the election. The county will notify the Silk Factory Guild in advance for their information.

Birthday Celebration Moves to Shilu: Mr. Shi Qinglin, Tianmin, Tiannong, Tianlu and his venerable father, Mr. Wei Ping, will celebrate his sixtieth birthday today (the 30th). Relatives and friends from far and near have generously offered birthday gifts. The Shi brothers have repeatedly declined but have been unable to refuse. Therefore, they have decided to use all the celebration funds to rebuild the section of Shijia Dang to Huajia Tian Bridge on the fifteenth route in order to facilitate transportation.

Changzhou 53

Military Police Corps Arrests Fake Battalion Commander: The Third Corps of the Military Police stationed in Changzhou received a secret report on the 27th that Wang Zhenguo from Xuzhou and others were posing as battalion commanders, abusing their authority to appoint officials, swindling people, collecting money to sell official positions, and gathering crowds for meetings. Sui Zongxi of the Corps dispatched a team to cooperate with the Public Security Bureau to search No. 1 Xiaotaiping Lane and found the fake battalion commander Wang Zhenguo and Song Hongpin, as well as smoking paraphernalia, letters, etc. They then went to the He Family Ancestral Hall on North Zhijie Street and arrested the fake adjutant Yang Senchang and the fake councilor Bu Kequan. They also found official seals at the Qianqiufang Cultural Society engraving shop. They were all arrested and interrogated by the Corps. Sui, the Corps’ agent, considering the seriousness of the case, sent a team to escort Wang Zhenguo and Song Hongpin to the Capital Garrison Headquarters on the night of the 28th for interrogation. The remaining two, Yang Senchang and Bu Kequan, will await further instructions from above.

Bandits First Rob Zhouqiao Town: At about 6 PM on the 27th, a bandit ship suddenly arrived at Zhouqiao Town in the Eighth District of Wuyi. It carried more than ten armed bandits who landed and searched house to house, killing Ye Tongyuan, a resident of the town, and injuring Zhang Shunlin and Liu Changyou. The reed mat boat on the river was also searched, and a coal boat was forced to follow. After investigation, it was found that the shops robbed included Yan Ruitai, Jin Xinghe, Hongzhengyuan, and Yongniantang. The District Chief and Town Head immediately reported the incident to the County Government on the 28th for investigation and arrest. The injured are currently being treated at Wujin Hospital.

Jiangyin 54

Resolutions of the Jiangsu-Changzhou Pacification Conference: The Jiangsu-Changzhou Pacification Zone held a meeting in Chengxiang on the 28th. Details have been reported in this newspaper. The meeting began at 9:00 AM, with sixteen representatives from the eight counties of Wuxi and Wu attending. Commander Zhu presided. More than twenty proposals related to bandit suppression were submitted, and the details of the resolutions were kept secret. The following are the resolutions published by the Headquarters: (6) If any armed group fails to provide assistance to neighboring areas when bandit alarms occur, the circumstances will be investigated and reported for punishment depending on the severity. (7) When suppressing bandits, if the bandits flee in a certain direction, the unit responsible for guarding that direction will be held responsible under military law. If there are special circumstances that need to be reported in advance, otherwise, if there are suspicious activities, the County Magistrates should report to the Headquarters for investigation and punishment. (9) The Jiangsu-Changzhou area is mostly a water region, bordering Lake Tai, with numerous rivers and streams, making it a key location for bandit activity. The most important strategy for prevention and suppression is to focus on water patrols. However, the number of water police teams is insufficient. Can each county expand the water patrol teams that have already been established? Or can they raise funds to establish regular patrols to supplement the water police and quell banditry? (15) During the purification period, the counties should thoroughly investigate and report to the Headquarters any privately held firearms or bandit weapons so that they can be forwarded for review and handling. (18) Counties without bandit disturbances should immediately assist the local purification bureau in carrying out purification. (19) For areas that have been cleared or counties without bandit disturbances where purification has been completed, the County Government should report to the Headquarters so that it can be forwarded. (20) Each armed group should submit a detailed report to the Headquarters every week on their daily bandit suppression activities and assistance with purification. If there are special circumstances, a report should be submitted immediately. (1) Temporary Proposal by the Wu County Government: Bandits in Lake Tai appear and disappear unpredictably. It is proposed to plan and establish a leading team to fundamentally suppress them in order to protect the inland towns. (2) Proposal by Wujiang, Taicang, and Wu Counties: Please send troops to station and maintain local security. The meeting adjourned at 5:00 PM. The representatives left Chengxiang one after another today (the 29th) and returned to their respective counties.

According to the German engineer's opinion, the Old Jiang Bridge should be rebuilt at Dadaotou, and the Xin Jiang Bridge should also be moved west to Lujia Daotou for the sake of proper planning. The total construction cost is approximately one million yuan. The engineer returned to Shanghai yesterday and will come to Ningbo again soon to measure the water depth for the purpose of planning. It is said that the bridge design will be automatic rotating. It is heard that half of the funding has already been secured in Shanghai.

Educational News Highlights

National Treasury Burden Per Japanese Student 61

Faculty of Law: Minimum... 180 yuan

Faculty of Medicine: Maximum... 2,090 yuan

Tokyo, 29th Telegram: According to a Ministry of Education survey, the total recurring educational expenses of the six Imperial Universities, six official universities, and eighty-one directly administered vocational schools in the third year of Showa (1928) was 43,050,128 yuan, of which the government expenditure was 29,185,609 yuan. The national treasury burden per student was the lowest for the Faculty of Law, at only 180 yuan, and the highest for the Faculty of Medicine, with Niigata Medical University spending 2,090 yuan per person, ranking first. It is also a comical phenomenon that the Faculty of Law, which receives the least government financial support, has the most difficulty in obtaining employment, while graduates of the Faculty of Medicine, which receive the most government funding, are uniquely popular.

Ministry of Education Pays Attention to Social Education Funding 62

Ordering Provinces and Cities to Raise Funds to Meet Standards

Those That Have Met Standards Will Be Rewarded Separately

The Ministry of Education will separately reward and commend provinces and cities whose social education funding for the 18th and 19th years (1929 and 1930) has met the standards. Those that have not met the standards will be ordered to promptly report their plans to increase funding. The document sent to the Provincial and Municipal Education Bureaus states:

It is necessary to ascertain and compile the amount of social education funding for each province and city for the 18th and 19th years. A form has been created and sent by telegram for compliance and reporting. Based on the original numbers reported by each province and city, a statistical summary table and a comparative ranking table have been created. According to the calculations in each table, the explicitly stipulated standard for social education funding to account for 10 to 20 percent of total education funding has been met by seven provinces and cities: Fujian, Hunan, Zhejiang, Jiangsu, Shaanxi, Hankou, and Nanjing. Although the standard amount has not been reached, the proportion is still above 5 percent for five provinces and cities: Yunnan, Hubei, Shandong, Henan, and Beiping. The remaining are far behind, with Shanxi Province at four per thousand and Rehe Province at one percent being the smallest. It has been investigated that during the period of political tutelage, social education is extremely important. The Ministry believes that the implementation of the cause depends on the fulfillment of talents, and especially on the fulfillment of funding. The Ministry has stipulated the percentage of social education as the standard for assessing the administrative performance of social education in each province and city. Fujian, Hunan, Zhejiang, Jiangsu, Shaanxi, and the two cities of Hankou and Nanjing have all been able to comply, which is deeply commendable. The fact that Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Fujian, Shaanxi, Henan, Liaoning, Heilongjiang, Yunnan, Guangdong, Nanjing, and other eleven provinces and cities increased their funding in the 19th year compared to the 18th year is also sufficient to prove their efforts. Among them, Zhejiang Province increased by 6.8 percent, Yunnan Province increased by 6.99 percent, Shaanxi Province increased by 4.51 percent, and Fujian Province increased by 4.44 percent, which is particularly commendable. However, there are also as many as eleven provinces and cities where funding was reduced in the 19th year compared to the 18th year. Among them, Hankou City decreased by 8 percent, Hunan Province decreased by 7.47 percent, and Shandong Province decreased by 3.3 percent. This phenomenon is particularly inappropriate. As for Shanxi and Rehe Provinces, their percentages are even smaller, and their undertakings are even more backward, so they should be promptly revitalized in order to advance. Now, at the time of preparing the budget for the 20th year (1931), all provinces and cities that have not selected the stipulated standard must strive to increase funding, and strive to ensure that social education funding for the 20th year is significantly increased, and should promptly prepare and submit a plan to increase social education funding for the 20th year for assessment. Those whose percentage has reached the stipulated standard but is lower than the previous year should also find ways to increase it so that it can progress year by year. In addition to separate orders, a summary table and a comparative ranking table, each with twenty copies, are hereby printed and distributed for compliance with this order.

Ministry of Education Investigates Unregistered Private Secondary Schools 63

Yesterday, the Ministry of Education sent a circular to the Education Bureaus of all provinces and cities to investigate and report on all unregistered private secondary schools in each province and city for verification. The circular states: It has been investigated that the deadline for the registration of private schools is the day before the start of the first semester of the 20th year (1931). The Ministry has previously issued orders to this effect. Recently, the educational administrative organs of various provinces and cities have successively submitted to the Ministry for filing a list of private secondary schools that have been registered, which is certainly very many. However, apart from the Guangdong Provincial Education Bureau, which has separately reviewed and approved the establishment of unregistered private secondary schools in the province and reported them to the Ministry for record, and the Rehe Provincial Education Bureau, which has reported that there are no unregistered private secondary schools, the Ministry has no way of knowing how many unregistered private secondary schools there are in other regions. Now that the deadline is imminent, it is hereby ordered again to expedite the investigation and clear reporting of the number and names of all unregistered private secondary schools under jurisdiction to the Ministry for filing. At the same time, unregistered schools should still be urged to complete registration procedures within the deadline. Those who deliberately wait and see and fail to apply for registration after the deadline should be strictly dealt with in accordance with the Ministry's Instruction No. 697 of July of the 19th year (1930). In addition to separate circulars, this order is hereby issued to the office for compliance with reporting.

Ministry of Education Revises Regulations for Vocational Schools 64

The regulations for vocational schools have now been revised and promulgated by the Ministry of Education on March 26 of the 20th year of the Republic of China (1931). The revised full text is reproduced below:

Chapter 1: General Principles

Article 1: The establishment of vocational schools shall be in accordance with the provisions of Article 1 of the Vocational School Organization Law, which states that the purpose is to teach applied science and train technical personnel.

Article 2: The length of study in vocational schools shall be two or three years, and each school may determine it separately according to its type, but it must be submitted to the Ministry of Education for approval. The length of study in medical vocational schools shall be three years, and after the completion of the courses, one year of practical training shall be required.

Article 3: The admission qualification for vocational schools shall be graduation from a public or registered private senior secondary school or an equivalent school, or have equivalent academic ability to a senior secondary school graduate, and pass the entrance examination. The number of students admitted with equivalent academic ability shall not exceed one-fifth of the total number of students admitted.

Article 4: The transfer qualification for vocational schools shall be that the schools are of the same nature, the level of the subjects is equal, and there is a certificate of study from the original school. The transfer must be before the start of the academic year or semester and pass the examination. However, students from unregistered private vocational or specialist schools shall not transfer to public and registered private vocational schools. Vocational schools shall not accept transfer students in their final year.

Chapter 2: Types and Curriculum

Article 5: The types of vocational schools are as follows: Class A (those with two or more of the following specialties may be called Industrial Vocational Schools): 1. Mining and Metallurgy Vocational School; 2. Mechanical Engineering Vocational School; 3. Electrical Engineering Vocational School; 4. Chemical Engineering Vocational School; 5. Civil Engineering Vocational School; 6. River and Ocean Engineering Vocational School; 7. Architectural Vocational School; 8. Surveying Vocational School; 9. Textile Vocational School; 10. Dyeing Vocational School; 11. Papermaking Vocational School; 12. Leather Making Vocational School; 13. Ceramics Vocational School; 14. Shipbuilding Vocational School; 15. Aircraft Manufacturing Vocational School; 16. Other vocational schools related to industry. Class B (those with two or more of the following specialties may be called Agricultural Vocational Schools): 1. Agronomy Vocational School; 2. Forestry Vocational School; 3. Veterinary Vocational School; 4. Horticulture Vocational School; 5. Sericulture Vocational School; 6. Animal Husbandry Vocational School; 7. Aquaculture Vocational School; 8. Other vocational schools related to agriculture. Class C (those with two or more of the following specialties may be called Commercial Vocational Schools): 1. Banking Vocational School; 2. Insurance Vocational School; 3. Accounting Vocational School; 4. Statistics Vocational School; 5. Transportation Management Vocational School; 6. International Trade Vocational School; 7. Taxation Vocational School; 8. Salt Affairs Vocational School; 9. Other vocational schools related to commerce. Class D: 1. Medical Vocational School; 2. Pharmacy Vocational School; 3. Art Vocational School; 4. Music Vocational School; 5. Physical Education Vocational School; 6. Library Science Vocational School; 7. Municipal Administration Vocational School; 8. Merchant Marine Vocational School; 9. Other vocational schools not belonging to Classes A, B, or C.

Article 6: Vocational schools may, according to their type, be attached to senior secondary schools of a vocational nature.

Article 7: Vocational school lectures may be divided into several groups when necessary.

Article 8: Party principles, military training, and Chinese language shall be compulsory courses for all types of vocational schools. The course allocation and curriculum standards for various vocational schools shall be determined separately.

Article 9: Vocational school courses may adopt a credit system, but the number of credits taken by students each semester must be limited and they may not graduate early (incomplete).

Local News

Xu Peihuang's Speech on the General Situation of Municipal Education 65

Yesterday, Xu Peihuang, Director of the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education, delivered a speech at the Shanghai YMCA on the general situation of Shanghai's educational administration. He stated briefly that the purpose of education, to put it simply, is not only to cultivate the ability to make a living independently but also to cultivate talents suitable for the social environment. Education is closely related to culture. The educational facilities in our country focus solely on material development, which will inevitably lead to mutual struggle in the future, and may still hinder cultural progress. Therefore, education must not only be suitable for the national environment but also be united with various countries in the world. Modern education in China is based on the Three Principles of the People, so that all Chinese people can understand the legacy of the Premier's Three Principles of the People and achieve the Great Harmony. The Three Principles of the People are quite suitable for China's

environment, so we should strive to achieve the goal. Education in Shanghai is very complex, unlike the education in major cities of other countries, which is very pure. In the Shanghai concessions, there are Chinese Children's Public Schools, church schools, as well as national, municipal, private schools, and private tutoring schools. Private tutoring schools have been banned, but some scholars who are compelled by hunger and cold still set them up. Therefore, the implementation of education based on the Three Principles of the People is very difficult in Shanghai. The schools run by foreigners naturally have different educational policies from our country, and the church schools are all for missionary purposes. The situations of other national, municipal, and private schools are also different. In the unregistered private schools, the education

is not carried out according to the educational policies. The schools in Shanghai are so complex. Here are the statistics of the number of schools: There are eight registered universities, five national universities, and one independent college registered in the eighteenth year, and eight unregistered ones, including three national and eight private. There are forty-five middle schools and seventy-three primary schools, sixty unregistered middle schools, and fifty-nine primary schools. Therefore, the primary task now is to promote and supervise registration to ensure compliance with the standards stipulated by the Municipal Bureau of Education.

There are two reasons why private schools cannot apply for registration: (1) The teachers are all part-time; (2) The problem of funding. Therefore, the Education Bureau now plans to find ways to enable all schools to register within a time limit, otherwise they will be banned. In terms of educational funding, according to statistics in the sixteenth year, the annual expenditure for kindergartens and primary schools was 2,139,812.4 yuan, for middle schools 1,621,165.2 yuan, for colleges and above 1,489,053 yuan, and for vocational and supplementary schools 245,685 yuan, totaling 5,496,224 yuan, accounting for 32.2% of the municipal government's expenditure for primary schools and kindergartens, and 6.3% for middle schools. According to the statistics in the nineteenth year, the current situation of municipal schools is: 185 primary schools, 5 middle schools, 52 mass education centers, 16 supplementary schools, 4 mass supplementary schools, 7 sports fields, 1 circulating library, and 1 science laboratory, with an expenditure of over 820,000 yuan. As for the number of students, there are 460 male and 320 female students in municipal middle schools, 4,990 senior and 25,990 junior students in municipal primary schools, 110 male and 180 female teachers. There are 650 male and 330 female students in municipal primary schools. The total number of school-age children in the city is 102,022, with 33,739 enrolled and 46,056 not enrolled, and 22,237 children who are not of school age are enrolled. It is estimated that only 42.6% of school-age children are enrolled (excluding concessions). According to the statistics of the nineteenth year, the expenditure of the bureau on educational administration accounts for about 17%. The total cost is 925,890 yuan. Finally, I hope that our municipal administration will become more and more developed, and that the sovereignty of education will be unified and cooperate with the concessions to implement education based on the Three Principles of the People in accordance with our national educational policies.

Two Giants of the American Baseball World 81

Bana Du: Van Croff Tuo Qiong Sheng

| Passed Away One After Another |

St. Louis, 28th - Telegraph - Mr. Bana Du, the highly reputable general director of the American Replicating Tournament in the baseball industry, passed away yesterday in Roche Sida. Before the departure of Mr. Li, Mr. Van Croff Tuo Qiong Sheng, the founder of the American Circulating Tournament and the benefactor of the American baseball world, also passed away here today at the age of sixty-seven. After founding the circulating tournament, Mr. Qiong Sheng served as the general director for twenty-seven years until 1927, when he handed over his position to Mr. Bana Du. He was a pioneer in the baseball world and was famous throughout the world. The annual World Baseball Championship is about to open in two weeks, and the two giants of the baseball world have passed away one after another, causing great shock to the American baseball world. The two have left an immortal contribution to the history of world baseball.
