New Voices of Silk Cocoon Dumping 88

Now that the business community has implemented the Gregorian calendar, the lunar calendar has been abolished. Therefore, the so-called end of March in previous years has been invisibly eliminated, and the provisions of the period ocean have no fixed standard. Yesterday it was heard from those who work in this field that the dumping of silk cocoon is mostly determined by the cocoon collecting period, with no so-called bottom of March or half of April. It is only agreed that a certain place will上簇(spin cocoons) on a certain day or出發(ship) on a certain day, then this

The period 洋(ocean) of the contract must be delivered, and the fee price shall be according to the agreed example. If the spot fees have轩轾(fluctuations) at the time, it will not be used as evidence. Rumor has it that some money shops and certain banks have dumped 300,000 to 400,000 contracts, with the regular period fee price being 7 qian 3 fen 4 li to 4 li half.

Yarn and Cotton

Yarn: Yarn Market Turned from Strong to Flat Last Week

The yarn market showed a strong upward trend at the beginning of last week, with rapid price increases. This was mainly due to the development of domestic demand. The price of imported yarn increased, and exchange rates were difficult to loosen, making it profitable to purchase domestic yarn in China. Japanese firms were actively seeking to purchase large quantities of Japanese yarn, leading to a significant shortage of Japanese yarn. Most of the yarn for August and September was sold out, prompting purchases of Chinese yarn. Shenxin and Yong'an factories exported a considerable amount of yarn, further tightening the market. A major merchant and powerful players held long positions, exacerbating the upward trend. The entire output of the Qingdao yarn factory was shipped to Japan, leaving no stock available locally. As a result, purchases were made in Shanghai, boosting business along Qingdao and Tianjin North Roads, creating a prosperous market. The highest price for standard yarn reached 172.3 taels. Towards the weekend, as March approached its final day, sellers released a large quantity of cheap yarn, impacting the market. New sellers concentrated their efforts, and although buyers had significant purchasing power, the overwhelming selling pressure proved difficult to resist. Many intended to go short due to the high base price and clear sales volume, making it difficult for the market to stabilize. Consequently, sellers collectively dumped their holdings, causing prices to fall by three to four taels in the near term and 167 taels in the long term. However, a certain manufacturer remained unusually calm, as their stock had already been sold out, and their internal organization was strong. Considering the surrounding environment, a major drop was unlikely. Nevertheless, the aggressive selling pressure from general short sellers temporarily impacted the market. Compared to the previous week, the price of standard yarn fell by one to two taels in the near term and seven to nine qian in the long term. Statistics show that various buyers purchased a total of 12,640 bales of spot yarn during the week, with Qingdao, Tianjin, and inland regions being the most active markets. Prices remained firm and high. It is reported that Shenxin and foreign firms also shipped five to six thousand pieces to Japan, but the exact number needs to be verified through customs records. The current period is during the peak spring sales season, and a large portion of purchases have not yet been made. Therefore, major players remain optimistic about the future. The actual direction of the market will depend on current sales trends. The total turnover of standard yarn for the week was 238,650 bales. Yesterday's Memorial Meeting for the Huanghuagang Martyrs 94

City Party Headquarters Assembly

Yesterday was the 20th anniversary of the sacrifice of revolutionary martyrs. The Propaganda Department of the Shanghai Special City Party Headquarters specially convened people from all walks of life in the city to hold a memorial meeting. Over three hundred representatives from more than one hundred groups attended. The meeting was chaired by Yang Qingyuan, Director of the City Propaganda Department, who reported on the martyrdom of the revolutionary martyrs and put forward three points to encourage the attending representatives. Representatives then delivered speeches one after another, speaking passionately and tragically. The following is a record of the various aspects of the meeting:

Chairman's Report Fellow Comrades, Fellow Representatives

Today is the 20th anniversary of the sacrifice of revolutionary martyrs, which is also the revolutionary memorial day of the most significant, most intense, and most influential sacrifices in the revolutionary movements before the Xinhai Revolution. Before the Opium War in 1842, the situation in China was unclear to the world. After the Opium War, China's weakness, political corruption, and the betrayal of officials were clear to all countries in the world. At the same time, the world's colonies were fully exploited by imperialists, and the world's small and weak nations were completely slaughtered by imperialists. Only our large and resource-rich China still stood in the East. As a result, international imperialists challenged us in every way and sought opportunities to exploit us. As a result of the various Sino-Japanese, Anglo-French, and other wars, China was burdened with territorial concessions and unequal treaties. After the Sino-French War, although Dr. Sun Yat-sen, the Prime Minister of our Party, and many revolutionary martyrs advocated revolution, the people were still ignorant and apathetic. Therefore, the first step for the revolutionaries was to awaken the people, hoping to use practical revolutionary movements and tragic sacrifices to awaken the general public. Since the "99" revolutionary movement, there were successive failures for several years, with more than nine failures. The number of party members who were martyred is unknown. However, the indomitable revolutionaries did not lose heart. Therefore, after the ninth revolutionary failure, Dr. Sun Yat-sen convened a secret meeting in Penang, British Malaya, with Mr. Huang Xing, Zhao Boxian, Hu Hanmin, and others. After negotiation, it was decided to convene the elite of the entire Party on March 15, 1910, for a final attack. Unexpectedly, on March 11, a shocking and sensational heroic act occurred, in which party member Wen Shengcai assassinated the Qing general Fu Qi, causing panic among Qing officials. Fearing the bravery and greatness of the revolutionaries, the city of Guangzhou was placed under special martial law, and the party's funds were not fully prepared. Therefore, it was decided to postpone the attack to March 29, which is today, twenty years ago. The plan was extremely meticulous, and the revolutionary troops were unaware. After the attack was launched at 5 p.m. on the 29th, it was attacked because the Qing officials were prepared and suffered mutual misunderstandings and infighting. The tenth revolutionary movement ended in a tragic failure. Those who participated in the attack were the most staunch revolutionary forces of the Party, and many were students who had returned from overseas. Therefore, the sacrifice was great and the loss was unprecedented. Guangdong is located in the tropics, and it was spring in March. The corpses of the martyred party members littered the streets, a tragic sight that caused tears. Fortunately, the righteous Mr. Pan Dazheng came forward and buried them collectively at Huanghuagang. We must know that the seeds of the Wuchang Uprising were deeply sown by the Huanghuagang Uprising. The revolutionary martyrs regarded death as returning home and taking righteousness as life. They did not simply hope to overthrow the Qing Dynasty, nor did they simply hope to hang up a signboard of the Republic of China. They demanded the establishment of a new China based on the Three Principles of the People of the people, by the people, and for the people. Although the warlords have been overthrown, reactionary elements are still lurking in various places, feudal forces are still rampant, bandits are still burning and killing in rural areas, and imperialists are still advancing step by step. Today, as we commemorate the martyrdom of the revolutionary martyrs, we should mourn the martyrdom of the revolutionary martyrs and consider how to continue their spirit and complete their unfinished will. I now put forward three points in the hope that everyone will work hard. First, we must complete the political tutelage and construction so that the Republic of China is not just an empty signboard and so that every citizen can exercise their political power and participate in national affairs. This all depends on whether the work of political tutelage can be completed. The reason why the Xinhai Revolution failed so tragically was that there was no period of political tutelage. The reason why Yuan Shikai, Zhang Xun, and all the warlords, large and small, were able to wreak havoc in the history of the Republic of China for more than ten years was that the people had no ability to exercise political power. Learning from the past, the work of the political tutelage period is truly important. Fellow Comrades, we are now at this critical juncture, and I hope that everyone will work hard. Second, we must continue the revolutionary spirit of the martyrs and strive to destroy the old and build the new. Whether we can thoroughly destroy and build depends on whether we have a full and rich revolutionary spirit. During the "2129" revolutionary movement, Mr. Zhu Zhixin was in another position, but when he learned of it, he immediately cut off half of his gown and rushed to kill the thieves. After Comrade Li Yanan was arrested, he asked for a bullet to enter his mouth and died by shooting himself. This heroic spirit of regarding death as returning home is the result of the deep cultivation of the revolutionary spirit. With this spirit, nothing is impossible. This is what every party member and every citizen should emulate. Third, the issue of the National Congress is the key to governing the country, because the construction cause can never be borne by the Kuomintang or the National Government alone. We must unite all the people to achieve success. The National Congress is the place to discuss the current major national affairs. However, the people of Shanghai seem to be too little concerned about the National Congress. It seems that whether the representatives are produced or not, whether the meeting is held or not, it is all the same. This kind of indifference to national affairs is truly worrying about the future of political tutelage. I hope that the representatives present will understand this and work hard to propagate to the people and continue the revolutionary spirit of the martyrs to build a new Republic of China. The report is over. Then the representatives delivered speeches one after another, which were mostly tragic, impassioned, and aroused the audience. The words are lengthy and

abbreviated.

Meeting Slogans (1) The spirit of the revolutionary martyrs is immortal (2) Continue the revolutionary spirit of the martyrs (3) Continue the sacrificial spirit of the martyrs (4) Complete the unfinished will of the martyrs (5) Eradicate reactionary elements (6) Eliminate feudal forces (7) Overthrow imperialism (8) Abolish all unequal treaties (9) Complete revolutionary construction (10) Realize the Three Principles of the People (11) Long live the Chinese Kuomintang (12) Long live the Republic of China

Municipal Finance Bureau Plans Business Tax Regulations and Detailed Rules 98

The various drafts of the city's business tax were previously passed by the Municipal Finance Discussion Committee in their first draft. After the Finance Bureau made significant revisions, the Business Tax Preparatory Committee presented them for discussion. It is reported that the draft regulations will soon be reviewed jointly with representatives from the Chamber of Commerce. Once finalized, they will be submitted to the Municipal Government for approval and referral to the Ministry of Finance for record. The full text of the draft regulations and detailed rules is recorded below:

(1) Draft Business Tax Regulations of Shanghai Municipality. Article 1: These regulations are established in accordance with Article 8 of the Outline for the Collection of Business Tax promulgated by the Ministry of Finance and supplementary regulations. Article 2: All operators within the city area listed in Article 4, except as otherwise provided by laws and regulations, shall be subject to business tax in accordance with these regulations. Article 3: Business operators meeting any of the following conditions shall be exempt from business tax upon verification: 1. Those with operating capital of less than 500 yuan; 2. State-owned or municipal enterprises; 3. Non-profit businesses. Article 4: The taxable standards and tax rates for business tax are specified separately in a schedule by category. Article 5: For the sale of goods, if it is wholesale, the business tax on the wholesale portion may be paid at one-quarter of the specified rate. The aforementioned wholesale business refers specifically to wholesalers in the same industry. If there is retail business in addition to wholesale, the tax amount shall still be calculated separately. Article 6: The calculation of operating capital shall be based on the actual paid-in capital and various (public reserve funds). Article 7: If various businesses have branches within the city, the business tax may be paid by the head office in a consolidated manner. If the head office or branch is located outside the city, tax shall be paid only for the branches or head office located within the city. If there is disagreement, it shall be handled in accordance with Article 13. Article 8: If a store engages in several types of businesses with different tax rates, the tax amount shall be calculated based on the primary business. Article 9: If manufacturers sell their manufactured products directly, the direct sale portion shall still be taxed at the current tax rate for the sale of goods. Article 10: For businesses with turnover or capital as the tax base, the estimated annual business income or capital amount shall be used to determine the total annual tax amount, which shall be divided into twelve months for monthly collection (the monthly collection amount is one-twelfth of the annual tax amount). For newly established businesses, business tax shall be calculated from the month of commencement. Article 11: All businesses listed in Article 4 shall, at the commencement of business tax, have the collecting agency dispatch personnel to investigate and register the following items and issue a business license. Thereafter, in the first month of the following year, the business operator shall complete and submit a report for the business license. For newly established businesses, the report shall be submitted before commencement, including: 1. Type and name of business and its location; 2. Name, origin, and address of the business operator; 3. Amount of operating capital; 4. Estimated annual business income. The aforementioned business license shall be renewed annually without a fee, but those meeting the tax exemption requirements of Article 3 shall pay a license fee of two jiao of silver. Article 12: For businesses with turnover as the tax base, the business operator shall settle the business turnover amount once every year in June and at the end of December, and must report it to the collecting agency before the 15th of the following month. However, if the business ends in less than six months, it shall be reported at the time of termination. Article 13: If the business operator fails to report truthfully in accordance with Articles 11 and 12, the collecting agency may dispatch personnel to investigate and verify the tax amount. If there is disagreement, the collecting agency shall submit it to the Finance Bureau for referral to the Review Committee for assessment. The same applies to disagreements with the decision of the collecting agency at the commencement of business tax. Article 14: The organization and review rules of the Review Committee shall be determined separately. Article 15: When collecting business tax, the collecting agency may inspect the business operator's account books, documents, goods, etc., when necessary, but it must be done in conjunction with the city's Chamber of Commerce. Without the approval of the Review Committee, the account books, documents, goods, etc., shall not be removed from the inspected store for investigation and inspection. Article 16: If the business operator closes, transfers, moves, reorganizes, or adds capital, etc., they shall immediately report to the collecting agency and surrender the old license and apply for a new one separately. Article 17: If the business license is lost or damaged, a new license shall be applied for, and a license fee of two jiao shall be paid. Article 18: If the business operator overreports or conceals business income or capital, operates without a license, or delays tax payment, once discovered or reported, in addition to paying the tax and obtaining a license in accordance with regulations, they shall be subject to penalties separately. The penalty rules shall be determined separately. Article 19: The Finance Bureau shall issue a monthly notice of business tax collection, and an annual credit record shall be compiled, reviewed, signed, and announced by the Review Committee. Article 20: All existing taxes and levies in the city that are similar in nature to business tax shall be renamed business tax and shall be collected temporarily at the old tax rates. Article 21: For businesses not listed in the schedule of Article 4 of these regulations but meeting the nature of business tax collection, the Finance Bureau shall formulate the tax rate to be collected and submit it for approval. Article 22: The detailed rules for the implementation of these regulations shall be determined separately. Article 23: These regulations shall take effect from the date of promulgation.

(2) Draft Detailed Rules for the Implementation of the Business Tax Regulations of Shanghai Municipality. Article 1: These detailed rules are established in accordance with Article 22 of the Business Tax Regulations of Shanghai Municipality. Article 2: The collection of business tax shall be handled by the Finance Bureau, considering local conditions, and separate offices shall be established. However, in special circumstances, it may be entrusted to other agencies. Article 3: All operators within the city area, regardless of whether they meet the requirements of the business tax regulations or not, shall comply with Article 11 of the Business Tax Regulations of Shanghai Municipality to apply for a business license. Article 4: Business operators shall keep account books recording the following items: 1. Detailed amount of goods and raw materials purchased; 2. Detailed amount of goods sold; 3. Daily cash receipts and payments; 4. Monthly totals; 5. Annual totals. Article 5: The collecting agency for business tax shall prepare a business tax register and classify and record the items in accordance with Article 11 of the Business Tax Regulations of Shanghai Municipality. The format of the register shall be determined separately. Article 6: The amount of business tax payable by the business operator shall be determined by the collecting agency upon review of the investigation report by the investigator or the report submitted by the business operator. Article 7: The amount of business tax payable by the business operator shall not be reduced or increased within one year after it has been determined by the collecting agency, unless otherwise provided by laws and regulations. Article 8: For businesses taxed according to the tax rate, even if the annual business income or capital amount is less than 1,000 yuan, the tax shall still be calculated based on the amount of 1,000 yuan. Article 9: The collecting agency for business tax shall fill out a monthly receipt for the payment and hand it over to the collector for collection. Article 10: The business operator shall hang the business license in a conspicuous place in the store for inspection. Article 11: The reporting form for the business license application shall be prepared and issued by the Finance Bureau, and the collecting agency shall use its format separately. Article 12: If the business operator disagrees with the tax amount, the collecting agency shall state the investigation in detail, and if there is evidence, submit it to the Finance Bureau in accordance with Article 13 of the Business Tax Regulations of Shanghai Municipality. Article 13: If the business operator's report on the taxable standard amount is certified by an accountant, the investigation procedure may be waived, but if the collecting agency has any doubts, it shall still be handled in accordance with Article 13 of the Business Tax Regulations of Shanghai Municipality. Article 14: Business tax shall be paid only on the commercial shares of businesses with official and commercial joint ventures. Article 15: These detailed rules

If there are any omissions, the Finance Bureau may revise them at any time and submit them to the Municipal Government for approval and record. Article 16: These detailed rules shall take effect from the date of promulgation.

Jiangsu Provincial Business Tax Regulations Under Review 99

Minhang Chamber of Commerce Petitions for Correction

Ministry of Finance Approves Review

The Minhang Chamber of Commerce of Shanghai County previously submitted a petition to the Ministry of Finance requesting prompt correction of the business tax collection regulations and implementation details formulated by the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Finance, as they exceeded the scope of the Ministry's outline. This was done to comply with the established case and alleviate the merchants' difficulties. It was reported in this newspaper. It is now learned that the Chamber has received a reply from the Ministry of Finance, stating, "The petition has been noted. The Ministry is currently reviewing the Jiangsu Provincial Business Tax Collection Regulations and will forward the finalized version to the Jiangsu Provincial Government for transmission to the Department of Finance for compliance. This is for your information."

Various Industries Petition for Business Tax Reduction 100

Jewelry Industry: There are over 80 jewelry businesses in this city.

There has been an organization of the same industry association, but there is no fixed standard for the size of capital, and there is no fixed scope for the amount of business. Most of the high-end goods are imported. According to the person in charge of the association, in the revised business tax regulations of the Ministry of Finance, the jewelry tax is 10 per thousand. The businessmen in this industry are unable to bear it because the goods are luxury goods, but the industry is not a luxury industry. Imported jewelry has been taxed as luxury goods by the Customs according to the import tariff. There is no luxury in the scope of business. Moreover, there is no fixed amount of capital and no standard for business. Taxing 10 per thousand is factually impossible. Therefore, letters have been sent to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and the Tariff Research Committee requesting discussion. A meeting of members will be convened to discuss ways to reduce the business tax and proceed accordingly. However, in terms of the scope of business, if the government reduces the business tax by 2 per thousand, it should be able to bear it.

Ham Industry: The Ham Industry Association previously stated that the 15 per thousand business tax rate set by the Ministry of Finance was too burdensome for its members, causing them to decline. It repeatedly appealed for a reduction and sent Cai Xiaohe and others as representatives to Beijing to petition and present their difficulties. In the revised Jiangsu-Zhejiang business tax regulations of the Ministry of Finance, the ham business tax is still 10 per thousand, while the taxes for most industries have been reduced. Although the ham industry has been reduced to 10 per thousand, it is still included in the highest level of business tax rates. The results of previous appeals and petitions are equal to zero. Therefore, a meeting of members will be convened again this afternoon (30th) at 3:00 pm to discuss and plan to send representatives to Beijing to petition as a final request.

Mayor Zhang's Remarks on Recovering Roads Built Beyond the Concessions 101

The Daily News reported that the National Government's Ministry of Foreign Affairs had negotiated with the ministers of the countries concerned regarding the incident of roads built beyond the Shanghai Concessions, but no results have been achieved. The Shanghai Municipal Government is also making great efforts to negotiate for recovery. Recently, the Concession authorities have met with Mayor Zhang at the Municipal Government several times to discuss the matter, but the extent of progress is rarely known to the outside world. Yesterday, a reporter from the Daily News visited Mayor Zhang to inquire about the progress of the negotiations. Mayor Zhang replied to the reporter, "The Concession authorities have indeed met with the Municipal Government several times to discuss the matter, but they were all informal talks. The main body of negotiations is the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the ministers of the countries concerned. However, the intention of this government is that all citizens of this country should exercise their sovereignty and absolutely cannot give up any of it. Recently, the police, finance and other rights have been recovered. As for the formalities of

negotiation, it is up to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs."

The Public Works Department Establishes a Real Estate Valuation Committee 102

Nominating Five Chinese and Foreign Committee Members

The properties in the Public Concession are often changed and improved, and their prices also rise accordingly. However, taxpayers often have disputes with the Public Works Department during valuation. In view of this, the Public Works Department has appointed five representatives of different nationalities to form a committee to adjudicate petitions regarding valuation disputes. In the past, owners could petition the Finance Committee of the Public Works Department for revaluation of land prices within the prescribed period, but there was no way to petition for revaluation of house prices based on rent. Therefore, the Public Works Department's move is convenient for the owners. The five committee members are Zhe Yanfang, Mr. Mizuta, Mr. Naisse, Mr. Louis, and Mr. Comrie. Except for Louis and Comrie, who were appointed by the Public Works Department, Zhe Yanfang was nominated by the Chinese Property Owners' Association, Mizuta was nominated by the Japanese Residents' Association, and Naisse will be the representative of the expatriates of various countries.

Report After the Far East Economic Study Group Arrives in England 103

What China Needs Now

Is Peace, Not Loans

The China Press reported from London on March 28 that Sir Thompson, leader of the Far East Economic Study Group, was very satisfied with the results of this trip. His report stated that what China needs now is peace, not loans. All members believe that the loan recently proposed by the United States to China will not help consolidate silver prices. However, this proposal has been withdrawn after the silver price has risen slightly. The members also believe that if the United Kingdom wants its commerce in the Far East to progress, it must place its commerce on a competitive basis.

Current Status of the Preparations for the International Trade Association 105

The International Trade Association was initiated and prepared by the former Ministry of Industry and Commerce. Its purpose is to bring together industrialists and economists from all over the country to study methods of foreign trade in order to develop international trade, and its nature is entirely an independent academic organization that is not affiliated with any party. According to the Preparatory Office, the internal organization system has been roughly scaled, and letters are now being sent to the preparatory members who agree with the association's purpose, inviting them to formally join as members. Once the formal replies of the members are received and the association's premises are secured, it can be officially established.

McGonagall Road Freight Train Derailment Last Night 106

Repaired This Morning

At around 7 pm last night, the B-9 freight train locomotive at McGonagall Road Station, pulling seven heavy cars, was intended to be sent from the E-character freight track No. 10 to the B-character freight warehouse No. 5. When the train reached the No. 26 turnout, the last three cars suddenly derailed. The traffic in the freight warehouse area was completely cut off. Fortunately, it was far from the main road, so the traffic between Beijing, Shanghai, and Hangzhou was not blocked. The North Road Engineering, Mechanical, and Traffic Departments have dispatched workers to repair it and dispatched a rescue vehicle. It is expected to be repaired at around 2 or 3 am this morning.

Reefs and Sunken Ships Discovered in the Yangtze River Basin 107

In the Yangtze River Basin, a sunken ship was suddenly discovered near Liuhai Sand North, 4 nautical miles away at 252 degrees north of the clock tower of Tiensheng Port Customs in Tongzhou. The ship's mast is still above the water surface. Reefs have also been discovered near the north of the Yangtze River estuary. Navigators are at risk if they are not careful. The Naval Hydrographic Office has urgently notified various shipping agencies to pay attention and surround the reefs exposed to the water surface with a circular danger line for navigation identification in order to know where to go.

Over 200 Japanese Fishing Boats Off the Coast of China 109

Since last summer and autumn, Japanese fishing boats have successively come to China to cross-border and invade fishing areas. Since our government did not stop them, and there are more than 4,000 new and old fishing boats in Japan, it is difficult for the fishing areas to accommodate them, and the fish species have been reduced. Therefore, they have crossed the sea to China to fish every day. According to the recent investigation by the fishing industry organizations in this port, there are more than 200 Japanese fishing boats in the seven coastal provinces from Northeast China to Guangdong, especially in Dalian, Qingdao, and Shanghai. Since the Customs has implemented the collection of fishing tax on foreign fishing boats and strictly cracked down on Japanese fishing boats imported as merchant ships, Japanese fishermen have been panicked and are requesting the Japanese government to negotiate with our government for relief.

This City's Fish Dealers Stop Selling Japanese Fish 110

To Maintain National Business

And Restore Lost Rights

Since the import and sale of Japanese Dongyang fish (also known as salted fragrant fish), it has flooded the whole country. In Shanghai alone, the total daily sales of each fish dealer is more than 10,000 yuan, which has reduced the sales of domestic salted fish. The fishermen in our country have suffered losses for years. Yesterday, it was heard that the fishermen in this port were planning to unite and join forces with the fish dealers in the South City to stop selling Japanese Dongyang fish in order to cope with the situation, maintain national business, and restore lost rights.

Aviator Mr. Ford Will Fly From Europe to China 111

The China Press reported that Mr. Ford, an employee of the Asia Petroleum Company stationed in Suzhou, took leave a few months ago to return to England to learn aviation in his spare time. He obtained a license at the beginning of this month and flew a Gibbsy Moth airplane alone from England on the 23rd of this month to the Far East. Yesterday, it was learned that he flew from Skokie near the capital of Yugoslavia to Sofia on Friday night. His parents have been working for the Inland China Mission for many years and are currently in Shanghai.

Four Suicides as a Result of Economic Oppression 116

Zhou Weichen and Yang Zhizheng are Dead

Zhang Rufeng was Fortunately Rescued After Being Discovered

Meng Baorong's Life is in Grave Danger

Zhou Weichen: Zhou Weichen, a 30-year-old man from Songjiang, resided at 834 Maigen Road. He had been unemployed for a long time. His wife, Ye Pinzhen, worked at the Boyi Yarn Factory, so she did not live with Zhou. They were husband and wife in name only. On the evening of the 26th of this month at 10:30 PM, Zhou suddenly had a suicidal thought and secretly consumed opium in his bedroom. When his housemate, Jin Apin, found out, he rushed him to the Red Cross Hospital, but the poisoning was too severe, and he soon died. The hospital notified the Gordon Road Police Station, which dispatched Detective Liang Yuliang to investigate. Zhou left two letters, which stated that he was committing suicide due to economic oppression and nothing else. The body was then taken to the Forensic Examination Office on Feilun Road. Yesterday morning, Guo Wei, a prosecutor from the Special District Local Court, arrived at the office. The coroner determined that Zhou Weichen died from self-administered opium poisoning. The body is being held for his mother to come to Shanghai for the encoffining and burial.

Yang Zhizheng: Yang Zhizheng, a 23-year-old man from Changzhou, had been unemployed for some time and had been drifting in Shanghai with no place to stand. He was staying at the Huachengxing Inn on North Zhejiang Road, unable to pay for his room and board. He felt a sense of despair and decided to swallow raw opium to commit suicide. When the poison took effect, he groaned. The inn reported it to the police, and Yang was sent to Jisheng Hospital on Baoshan Road for treatment, but he died. Yesterday, Yan Liugen, the local security officer of Jiyitu, reported the death to the Local Court for examination. It was approved and the body was encoffined for burial.

Zhang Rufeng: Yesterday morning, around 3 AM, before dawn, a young man suddenly came to the Dada Wharf on the 16th pier in Nanshi. He was elegantly dressed, but his eyebrows were tightly furrowed, and his face was full of unspeakable pain. As he gradually walked to the edge of the pier, he was about to jump into the Huangpu River when Guo Xiushi, a patrolman from the 1st District General Office Pier Police Station, spotted him and immediately rushed over and grabbed him. He was taken back to the station for preliminary questioning. The young man burst into tears and said that his name was Zhang Rufeng, he was 32 years old, a native of Ningbo, and lived at No. 72 Wengjia Lane inside the Old West Gate. He was engaged in the cloth business and was suffering from economic oppression and family discord. He felt that there was no joy in his life and wanted to commit suicide by jumping into the river. He was ordered to stay and arrangements would be made to settle him down.

Meng Baorong: The Hongkou Grand Hotel was visited by a guest on the afternoon of the day before yesterday at around 4 PM. The bellboy led him to room 85. The register showed that the guest was Meng Baorong, a 19-year-old man from Wuxi. He paid for the room and sat for a moment before going out to visit friends. He returned around 7 or 8 PM in the evening and went to bed. He didn't get up until noon the next day. The bellboy was very surprised and called out his name outside the door several times, but there was no response. He immediately found a way to pry open the door and saw Meng lying stiff on the bed, barely breathing. A diary was found on the bedside table with a suicide note. The handwriting was very messy and difficult to copy, but the general content stated that he was at odds with his father, left his hometown and came to Shanghai. He often read newspapers that mentioned a certain great philanthropist on the sea who was kind and generous. He packed his bags and set off, intending to visit a philanthropist after arriving in Shanghai and ask for his help. However, he was unfamiliar with the place and could not find him anywhere. He looked back at his empty wallet and felt that the future was bleak. He was ashamed to go home and had no way to make a living in Shanghai. He had no choice but to leave the world. The hotel accountant was informed and immediately ordered the bellboy to call the police and send Meng to Tongren Hospital for treatment. It is said that Meng took too much poison and his life is in danger.

Pig Industry Recovers Customs Duties for Self-Reporting 117

Effective April 1st

The Shanghai Pig Industry Dunren Association, considering that the various tax reporting firms in Wusong charge exorbitant and unreasonable fees for live pigs shipped from Tianchenggang and Zhanghuanggong and other ports in Jiangbei to Shanghai via Wusong, causing delays. They submitted a request to the Customs Tax Department to recover the customs duties for live pigs for self-reporting. The Tax Department approved the request. The Dunren Association is now sending staff to set up a pig industry transportation office and customs declaration office on the eastern section of the Wusong Outer Bund, appointing Zhao Shaozhai, the former director of the pig tax bureau, as the director, to handle the procedures. The self-reporting of customs duties will take effect from April 1st. The directors of the association, Pan Ziwen and Shen Mengxian, hosted a banquet at the New Hotel last night to invite officials from the Wusong police and representatives from the pig industry to strengthen communication and facilitate transportation.

Public Works Bureau Reorganizes Nanshi Wharves 119

Nanshi has always been known for its bustling atmosphere. In recent years, the shipping industry has flourished and the market has become even more prosperous. Last year, the Municipal Port Affairs Bureau was ordered to be abolished, and the Municipal Government took back the various ship wharves south of the 16th Pier and assigned them to the jurisdiction of the Public Works Bureau. A wharf warehouse management office was established outside Maojia Lane on the Bund, and Xu Yuanfang and Gao Shu'an were appointed as director and deputy director. Since taking office, Xu and Gao have been diligent in their work and have made every effort to plan and reorganize the wharves. All the existing moldy and damaged wooden piles and curved iron bars have been repaired and replaced, and more than 100 street lights have been added. This not only facilitates the loading and unloading of goods but also benefits travelers getting on and off ships. Dockworkers are required to wear numbered uniforms to carry goods, and water and land police patrol closely to supervise and manage them diligently. Petty thieves have disappeared, and the order is well-maintained. Travelers praise the improvements.

China Harmonica Association Seeks New Members 120

The China Harmonica Association at No. 168 Sichuan Road in Shanghai was founded by harmonica expert Wang Qingxun and several enthusiastic comrades. Since its establishment, it has attracted more than 350 members from all walks of life. Various schools in Shanghai have requested the establishment of branches, and there have been numerous requests from other places for correspondence courses and performances. The association's business is developing rapidly. The facilities are complete, and the teaching is serious. Four terms have been completed with excellent results. In order to popularize harmonica music and promote elegant arts, a "Fifth Elementary Harmonica Class" will be added. There will be day and night classes and a special noon class (every Monday, Tuesday, Thursday, and Friday from 1 PM to 2 PM, completed in one month) to facilitate the participation of interested parties from all walks of life. The tuition fee is very low, and regulations are printed and available.

Failure to Report Births Must Be Severely Punished 122

The Municipal Health and Public Safety Bureaus jointly issued a public notice yesterday, stating: "It is hereby announced that the statistics on births and deaths are extremely important for comparing population growth rates and for hygiene and sanitation facilities. Since this bureau has been handling this statistics, many families have repeatedly failed to report births, leading to a large discrepancy between the number of births and deaths each month. We have repeatedly issued earnest announcements and ordered the police to provide reminders at all times. However, our words have gone unheeded. The majority of families who have had births believe that this matter is not easily detectable, so they wait and see, disregarding the government's orders. If this continues, not only will population statistics be inaccurate, but hygiene and sanitation facilities will also lose their standards. After discussions between the Municipal Health and Public Safety Bureaus, it has been decided that in the future, regarding births, on the one hand, obstetricians, midwives, and delivery nurses will be responsible for reporting the facts of deliveries each month. On the other hand, each district office will be ordered to conduct thorough inspections and cross-reference the data at any time. If a family conceals a birth, they will be severely punished in accordance with the regulations. If the delivering personnel violate the regulations and fail to report or report falsely, they will be punished for violating the police regulations once discovered. The order will be carried out to the letter without any leniency. Therefore, we jointly issue this announcement, urging all citizens to abide by it without fail. This announcement is issued on March 29th, the 20th year of the Republic of China."

Huan Longbao's Wife 126

Was She Marrying through a Matchmaker?

Or Was She Abducted?

Huan Longbao from Xinghua was previously accused by Xu Binglong from Gaoyou of abducting his daughter, Xu Zhaodi. Huan insisted that Zhaodi was his wife. Both parties held their ground. The Special District Local Court decided to send letters to Xinghua and Gaoyou counties to ask for clarification for verification. The two counties have now replied to the Special Court. Xinghua replied that Zhaodi was indeed Huan's wife. Gaoyou replied that the detailed report submitted to the authorities did not contain the name of the Huan family's house or land, and there was no way to find out any other information. The Special Court continued to hear the case the day before yesterday. The plaintiff, Xu Binglong, was absent, which showed that his claims were false. Judge Xiao questioned Zhaodi, who testified that she was originally from Dongxiang, Gaoyou. In December of last year, she was abducted from the fields where she was drawing water by Huan and his relative, Sun Fulan, to Shanghai. She had never married Huan before. Huan still claimed that he was engaged to Zhaodi on February 16th of last year and married her on August 16th, with Yao, Wang, and Gao as matchmakers, and the dowry was 90 yuan. Judge Xiao ordered the defendant to be taken into custody for further investigation and verification.

Robbers Intercepted a Car 127

Min Shuliu and his Concubine were Watching a Movie

Loss of More Than 700 Yuan

Min Shuliu, a well-known trauma doctor residing in Yongnian Lane on Baik Road, was riding with his beloved concubine by car to the department store on Fada Road at 10 PM the night before last. They were planning to watch a movie at the Jiuxing Cinema on Changbang Road in the French Concession. They fled with the stolen goods.

Local News Two

Large Number of Ancient Bottles Discovered in Liuhekou 134

Divided into Korean Bottles and Qi Bottles

Most of the residents of 72 Village in Liuhekou, Taicang County, are engaged in fishing. Recently, fishermen in the area have caught a large number of pottery ancient bottles while fishing with corner hooks in the sea mouth. They are divided into two types: Korean bottles and Qi bottles. Korean bottles have four ears, and Qi bottles have two ears. The ears have holes that can be used to thread ropes. It is said that these ancient bottles were used by Han Shizhong of the Song Dynasty after Gaozong crossed south to quell the Miao rebellion to hold wine and reward soldiers. During the Jiajing period of the Ming Dynasty, Qi Jiguang also used this method after using Zhejiang soldiers to quell the Japanese pirates. After the soldiers drank all the wine, they threw the empty bottles into the sea. The bottles are divided into three sizes: large, medium, and small. Large bottles are about two feet high, medium bottles are about one foot high, and small bottles are five or six inches high. The diameter of the mouth is very small. The style is similar to the current thermos bottles, but the belly is slightly bulging. The texture is very rough and has swirl patterns. The bottom is slightly pointed. Large bottles can hold ten catties of wine, medium bottles can hold five catties, and small bottles can hold two catties. Fishermen obtain them and sell them in the market. Those who are curious buy and collect them. Small bottles cost four corners of a silver dollar each, medium bottles cost six corners, and large bottles cost one dollar. It is a pity that few of these ancient bottles are complete because fishermen need to hook the ear holes of the bottles with rolling hooks to lift them up, and after many years, the bottles are full of sea sand. When they are lifted out of the water, they are extremely heavy. If they are not careful, the bottle ears will fall off and it will be difficult to lift them up. Therefore, most of the bottles obtained have incomplete ears. The reporter is also one of the curious people who have seen these bottles but has no knowledge of antiquities. Therefore, I record this to await the textual research of antiquities scholars. According to the elders in the area, these ancient bottles are discovered every year, but not many. This year, the fishermen in the village have obtained hundreds of them, all of which were lifted from Liuhekou. It is thought that they have been washed away by sea tides over the years. It is said that if they are used to grow flowers, they can last for a long time.

Suspect in the Old Case, Nie Dianbang, Found Not Guilty 135

Jiangning Local Court Concludes Investigation

Insufficient Suspicion, No Prosecution

Nie Dianbang, father of the deceased Kunqu actress Qin Qiufang, was previously accused by Han Yaozhong, Yao Zhengyang, and others of the Shanghai Jiangsu River Police Team as an accomplice in the assassination of martyr Chen Ying shi in the fifth year of the Republic of China. He was then transferred by the General Headquarters Military Law Department to the Jiangning Local Court for investigation. The investigation by the procuratorate concluded that the suspicion was light, and he was temporarily granted bail. This newspaper has repeatedly reported on this. It is now learned that the court has concluded a careful investigation and decided not to prosecute Nie Dianbang. The full text of the disposition is transcribed below:

Non-Prosecution Disposition Jiangsu Jiangning Local Court Prosecutor's Non-Prosecution Disposition No. 758, Year 20. Defendant: Nie Dianbang (aka Nie Zhenbang), male, 42 years old, from Yutai County, Shandong Province, performer. The defendant's case of suspected homicide, Jianzi No. 4770, Year 19 of the Republic of China, has been investigated by this prosecutor. This office believes that no prosecution should be filed. The facts and reasons are now stated below. Nie Dianbang is the father of the late Kunqu actress Qin Qiufang. On April 20th, Year 5 of the Republic of China (March 18th of the abolished calendar), Dianbang escorted Qiufang and her cousin Qin Xuefang from Shanghai to Little Luzon to perform. They only returned to China in the autumn of the following year. Unexpectedly, after fifteen years, Han Yaozhong and Yao Zhengyang accused Dianbang of being an accomplice in the assassination of martyr Chen Ying shi in Shanghai on May 18th, Year 5 of the Republic of China, and that he had recently arrived in Shanghai with conspiracies and unruly intentions. The report was made by Zhang Zhaoxiang, detective chief of the Fourth District of the Jiangsu River Police Team, who arrested Dianbang on January 6th of this year. The case was transferred by the Military Law Department of the General Headquarters of the Army, Navy, and Air Force, and the Judicial Yuan instructed the Ministry of Judicial Administration to issue an order for investigation. The case was investigated according to law, and it was concluded that no prosecution should be filed.

The Reasons: (A) The testimonies of Han Yaozhong and Yao Zhengyang are not credible. According to the records, Han Yaozhong and Yao Zhengyang stated before the military judge of the Military Law Department of the General Headquarters of the Army, Navy, and Air Force on January 18th of this year: "At that time (referring to May 18th, Year 5 of the Republic of China), I lived upstairs in the alley entrance of Xinminli, Bairbu Road. They (referring to Nie Dianbang and others) were six or seven people who often went to a tailor shop to make clothes. That day, we were chatting when we heard gunshots on the road. We ran downstairs to the alley entrance and saw them running away towards the open space across from Xinminli, heading west. Nie Dianbang and Wu Baoxian were also together," and so on. Yao Zhengyang's testimony was similar. When this court entrusted the Shanghai Special District Local Court to summon Han Yaozhong for questioning, he said, "I was a partner in a clothing store in Xinminli. That day, many people were walking around the alley entrance, including Nie Dianbang and Wu Guohua (aka Wu Baobao), because they often came to my store to have clothes made, so I recognized them." Regarding the previous statement that Nie Dianbang often went to a tailor shop, upon close examination, that shop was not Han Yaozhong's place of work, but merely a statement of what he saw from the alley upstairs at the time. However, according to the later statement that Nie Dianbang often came to my store, it seems that Nie Dianbang frequently went to Han's place and was well known to Han. If Han Yaozhong did have firsthand knowledge of the assassination of Chen at that time, why would his statements regarding his own position be inconsistent? Furthermore, the submitted diagram clearly states that the murderers Nie Dianbang and others fled west (the open space at the west end of Bairbu Road and Pushi Road), which is clearly different from the eyewitness account of Shen Zuyin (Mr. Chen Ying shi's bodyguard), who said that the murderers fled out the back door of No. 14 Sapo Sai Road, heading east to Sapo Sai Road and then south. Moreover, Han Yaozhong previously said that Chen was killed outside the entrance of the Xinminli alley, but later said that Chen was killed inside the Xinminli residence, which is inconsistent with Shen Zuyin's statement that Chen was assassinated in the reception room of Sapo Sai Road (which is consistent with the facts recognized in the previous confirmed judgment of the Shanghai Local Court). All of these factors lead to the conclusion that the testimonies of Han and Yao are not credible. (B) Nie Dianbang had already gone to Little Luzon before the day Chen was assassinated. According to the investigation, Nie Dianbang went to Little Luzon in April of the fifth year of the Republic of China. The testimonies of Nie Dianbang and his wife Nie Hao shi were consistent and unwavering. Furthermore, the Shanghai French Concession Joint Court confirmed in its reply that Nie Dianbang was not in Shanghai when martyr Chen Ying shi was assassinated on May 18th of that year, so he could not have been a suspect. (C) There is no active evidence of Nie Dianbang's crime. Nie Dianbang has been thoroughly interrogated by the Military Law Department of the General Headquarters of the Army, Navy, and Air Force and this court, and it is confirmed that he did not assassinate Chen. Furthermore, the Shanghai Special District Local Court was requested to interrogate the prisoner Wu Baobao (reported by Han Yaozhong and others as Nie's accomplice) in the theft case, and it was confirmed that he did not assassinate Chen with Nie. As for the newspaper report that Nie Dianbang was the escaped prisoner in the Chen assassination case, the military judge of the Military Law Department personally visited Zhao Yuhuang and Peng Qi, the judges of the first and second instance of the case in Shanghai, and Qin Liankui, the lawyer appointed for defense, and presented Nie's photo to them for identification. They all said that he was definitely not the principal offenders Xu Guolin and Su Zhenfang at the time. Moreover, Xu and Su were already over fifty years old, while Nie was only forty-two years old. Since their ages and appearances were different, it can be concluded that he was not an alias of Xu and Su. In conclusion, the defendant Nie Dianbang does not have sufficient criminal suspicion. Therefore, according to Article 244, Paragraph 2 of the Criminal Procedure Law, a decision not to prosecute is made. Prosecutor Ouyang Shu, March 23rd, Year 20 of the Republic of China. This document is certified to be identical to the original. Clerk Zhao Baoqing.

Sea Bandits Extort Flag Fees 136

120 Yuan Per Boat

Fishing Boats Request Suppression

Sea bandit leaders Zhong Dakui, Yan Zhenlin, Fu Damou, and others, with their remaining bandit gangs of about 400 men, are looting merchant ships in coastal ports and holding people for ransom. Recently, they have been taking advantage of the fishing season to force fishermen to pay a flag fee of 120 yuan per boat. If they do not pay, the boats will be seized and fishing will be prohibited. The fishermen are finding it difficult to cope with the simultaneous extortion by the three bandit gangs, and the spring fishing season is the most crucial time of the year. Therefore, yesterday, they sent representatives to the Wusong Coastal Defense Office and the Fourth District of the Wusong River Police to request suppression in order to maintain their livelihoods.

Seventy-Year-Old Woman Accuses Grandson of Being Beaten to Death 137

River Police Forcibly Claim Cotton as Small Goods

Private Torture Leads to Grandson's Death

Xu, the captain of the Shanghai Public Security Bureau's River Patrol Team, received a complaint yesterday afternoon from Luo Yang shi, an elderly woman of seventy years old, who lives on a boat at Yong Sheng Wharf and makes a living by boating. On January 16th of this year, Wu Xing Flower Shop (operated by Chen Tianxi, municipal commissioner of Yangsi Township) in Yangjing Town, Pudong, entrusted me to transport 150 packages of flower clothing from the shop to another port. I immediately loaded the cargo and set off with my grandson Luo A'gen. Unexpectedly, when the cargo ship passed through Wusong, it was spotted by patrols of the Fourth District of the Jiangsu River Provincial Public Security Team, who stopped us and forcibly claimed that it was small goods. We were taken to the district and forced to confess where we had stolen it. We truthfully explained the situation, but we were accused of lying and my grandson Luo A'gen was subjected to private torture, causing him to be covered in injuries. Then, we were transferred to the Shanghai Local Court. After the court investigated and found that we were indeed law-abiding citizens and that the flower clothing was indeed from Wu Xing Flower Shop, we were released and returned home on the 28th of this month. After returning, the injuries that A'gen had sustained from the Fourth District suddenly flared up and he died despite medical treatment. His body was completely purple. Recalling that my grandson A'gen was forcibly beaten to death by the Fourth District, leaving me with no recourse, I am requesting justice. The captain, recognizing the importance of the case involving human life, ordered the local neighborhood chief to report to the Local Court for an autopsy before further investigation.

Young Girl Enters Nunnery to Become a Nun 138

Suffers Constant Abuse from Stepmother

Father and Daughter Weep Upon Meeting

Jiang Liang sheng, a businessman from Sanlintang, Pudong, who deals in foreign goods, has two daughters. The eldest daughter is already married, and the younger daughter, Pei Hua, is twenty-one years old and unmarried. Jiang's wife died of illness two years ago, and the family lacked someone to take care of them. Therefore, last summer, relatives arranged a marriage for him with a woman surnamed Wu from Yangjiadu as his stepmother. After she entered the home, Pei Hua and her stepmother often had conflicts over family matters, so the mother and daughter rarely spoke to each other. Recently, another quarrel broke out. A few days ago, Pei Hua left home and crossed the river to Shanghai to buy silk and satin at Xiaodongmen. She returned home a little late and was reported to her father by her stepmother. Jiang immediately questioned Pei Hua. Pei Hua, feeling that her stepmother was instigating the situation and causing her father to humiliate her, quarreled with her stepmother again. However, Jiang protected his wife and scolded his daughter. Pei Hua, feeling resentful after being humiliated, suddenly left home on the 22nd of this month, taking all her jewelry with her and leaving a letter at home stating that she was now a nun and would not return home, asking her father not to worry about her. Jiang learned of this and asked people to inquire at various nunneries. Until the day before yesterday, Jiang was informed that there was a young woman at the Wanshou Nunnery in Zhabei who was apprenticing to a nun. Jiang went to the nunnery yesterday to search for her. After waiting for half a day, he saw the woman coming from inside to the main hall. Jiang stepped forward to identify her and it was indeed his daughter. Father and daughter wept uncontrollably upon meeting, which was very sad. Jiang asked his daughter to return home, but she resolutely insisted on becoming a nun and told her father, "Please don't worry about me, Father. It is better for me to practice here than at home. Please go home quickly." Jiang tried to persuade her repeatedly, but to no avail, and could only return in tears. Jiang has now asked his daughter's sister to persuade her to return home, but it is unknown if she will succeed.

A Few Words 143

— Xu Xiaoting

▲ A single telegraph pole can withstand the ravages of wind and rain, but a weak youth cannot withstand the pressures of the environment.

▲ A woman who is good at telling other people's love stories is not necessarily strict about keeping her own love story a secret.

▲ A cigarette can be offered to a guest casually, but a vulgar word cannot be casually spoken in front of a guest.

▲ When telling jokes to children, you don't have to be serious. When telling jokes to a lover, you must be careful.

▲ It is better to read interesting newspapers than to read useless supernatural novels.

▲ The wealthy are constantly afraid of being robbed by bandits, but the wealth in the belly of a scholar is not coveted by bandits. It can be seen that reading is the most advantageous thing in the world.

▲ Women are like flowing water. Flowing water can save lives when needed, but it can also cause death.

▲ People use flashlights to walk because they are convenient for providing light. However, our pursuit of a little knowledge for intellectual convenience is a hundred times higher than using a flashlight to light up the night.

The Flow of the Three Seals of Abdication to Foreign Lands 144

— Gong Yu

The Seal is also called the Qin Seal. Since Emperor Qin Shi Huang, the seal has been used as the emperor's seal. Before the Qin Dynasty, the use of seals on documents as proof of authenticity was not limited to the noble and lowly and was commonly called Seal Writing. The Zuo Zhuan says, "Ji Wu zi sent Gongye to ask for the Seal Writing, pursued him, and gave it to him," which is one example. Emperor Qin Shi Huang obtained the Heshibi jade and had Prime Minister Li Si write "Appointed by Heaven, May He Live Long and Prosper" and carved it into a seal, which became a treasure passed down through generations. When Ziying surrendered to the Han, he presented this seal to Gaozu. Later, when Wang Mang usurped the throne and the various pretenders of the Wei and Jin dynasties, they all fought for the seal because it had the words "Appointed by Heaven" and they used obtaining the seal as a sign of approval. Its gains and losses and the changes in its origins are detailed in Cui Yu's Memorial on the Hereditary Seal. Since Emperor Shun fled, this seal was lost again and its whereabouts are unknown. In the thirteenth year of Hongzhi in the Ming Dynasty, a resident of Hu County said that he had obtained this seal and presented it to Emperor Xiaozong, but he did not use it. The authenticity of the seals passed down through the generations cannot be known. During the reign of Emperor Taizong of the Qing Dynasty, this seal reappeared. Fan Wencheng said that Emperor Shun of the Yuan Dynasty was forced by the Ming army to carry the seal out of the country and eventually died in Yingchang. The seal's whereabouts were also unknown. Later, a shepherd in the hills saw a sheep that did not eat for three days and used its hooves to dig in the ground. It discovered the seal and returned it to the Yuan descendant Bosuoketu Khan. It was transferred to Lin Dan and then returned to Emperor Taizong, who regarded it as a good omen for entering the customs to replace the Ming Dynasty. However, it is uncertain whether it was the original Qin seal. This publication previously reported that this seal was found in a foreign country (I don't remember which country). It was seized by a sailor in the palace when the Allied forces entered Beijing in the Gengzi year. Later, due to a lack of funds for the journey, he sought to sell it to someone, but the Chinese consulate bought it and planned to return it to the Qing court. However, a revolution broke out in the country and it was not successful. It is now still stored in the home of a certain overseas Chinese. Recently, I heard from a friend that there are still several seals flowing overseas, all of which were carved during the Qianlong period of the Qing Dynasty. One is the Supreme Emperor's Abdication Seal, made of green jade with a turtle-shaped handle, half an inch long. One is the Supreme Emperor's Abdication and Continued Instruction Seal, made of green jade with a turtle-shaped handle, also an inch and a half long. One is the Wishes Fulfilled Seal, made in an oval shape. All three seals are in seal script and are stored in a box. The Qianlong period was the most prosperous era of the Qing Dynasty. Military achievements and cultural education both surpassed the past, and Emperor Gaozong's long reign was rare in history. Although Emperor Shengzu also reigned for sixty years, Emperor Gaozong still reigned for four years after abdicating before he died, truly worthy of being called the Perfect Emperor. Emperor Gaozong said that when he first ascended the throne, he swore to heaven that he only wished to reign for sixty years and dared not exceed the number of years Emperor Shengzu was in power. If he exceeded sixty years, he would abdicate. In fact, Emperor Gaozong was fond of grand achievements and spent his life enjoying glory, wealth, and honor to the extreme. Because he could not add more, he made the abdication an event within the dynasty and became the Supreme Emperor, regarding the emperor as even more honorable. His oath to heaven was just a pretext. Therefore, the extravagance and pomp at that time were beyond description and can be seen from these three specially carved seals. Now they have flowed to foreign lands, serving only as materials for museums, which is truly enough to make people feel the sense that the heroes of a generation are now nowhere to be found.

Inscriptions on the顨盦Collection 145

— Lian Nanhu

After the passing of Deng Guangwen of my hometown, people everywhere searched for his remaining manuscripts but knew nothing about them. Recently, I met his nephew, Zhu Jichi, who informed me that there were three volumes of his poems and lyrics in Wuchang. I searched and found them and was overjoyed and unable to sleep. I am proofreading a copy to entrust to printers to pay tribute to him with poetry and report it to Han Ya.

Lonely lamp transcribes manuscript, both calligraphy and sincerity, handling a thousand years of sorrow, a heart-stirring spirit. Dreams of singing and calling become a world away, Jiang Guan desolate has a successor. (The poem sent to Ji Chi says: There is a fine nephew who is very similar) Occasionally talk about flowers and moon, the body is weary, the upper air is thin, the unrestrained spirit is naturally pure. Helping the drunken win the past, now nearly exhausted, how many dust does Jiu Yuan see on the sea? (Thirty years ago, I once invited Gong and Yuan Zhang, Minister of the Province, Qin Wuqi, and Nong to get drunk on a painting boat on Ronghu Lake. There was a horizontal plaque hanging with the words "Sunset Xiao Drums." Gong smiled and said to me, "This is Chen Zhuangyuan's calligraphy." Wu Niang heard this and was quite proud. The moon rose on a cold night, and we helped each other home in a drunken state, which was a memorable event at that time. Now, Gu Zhang and Qin Wu are both buried with grass, and my stomach aches every time I pass the state gate.)

Sima Lingyun is not easy to climb, and his high name should be ranked with the ancients. (Yu Zhai's wall hangs a couplet by Bachelor Shanzhou, with the inscription 顨庵. Gong saw it and was very happy, saying that it coincided with his pen name, so he used it as a birthday gift) I was surprised to see it for the first time at Hongsheng Shop, and I looked for the old inscription by the Yingdong Lake. (I first met Gong at Hongsheng Shop in Xuan Nan. The next day, Gong visited me at the Yiguan to talk about the anecdotes of Ye Yuanli, saying that he had seen Yuyang's manuscript with the phrase "transformed into seventy-two mandarin ducks," which refers to this. After that, I checked the collection and could not find it) How dare I be a later generation of Ziyun? I left office and was lost in the path of Yuanliang. (My late uncle, Wu Kangzhi, retired from office and returned to seclusion, comparing himself to Tao Yuanliang. He built Juyin Villa between Longmian and Fudu. He died only five days after returning home. Gong selected and described a volume of Juyin Villa's remaining poems, saying that it is sad to say that there is no knowledge in the yellow soil and the silent blue code is of no benefit to the underworld.) The fishing companions have white heads, cutting paper to summon the soul until the sun sets in the west.

Anecdotes from the Preparatory Meeting of the Central National Medical Center 146

— Song Lu

The origin of our country's medicine has been a long time, but because the people of the country stick to conventions and do not know how to improve, it has gradually disappeared and lost its true tradition. Instead, Western medicine has flooded the market, and the economic invasion suffered every year is truly regrettable. After the late Director Tan proposed it, it was decided at the political conference to hand it over to the Executive Yuan to establish a Central National Medical Center, modeled after the Central National Martial Arts Center. Jiao Yitang and others were appointed to organize a preparatory committee. After several months of preparation, the outline has been determined, and famous doctors from various places have been invited to be initiators. The preparatory meeting was held in Beijing on the 17th of this month, and the talent was so great that it was a grand event. I was invited by a friend to go and watch, so I will describe the trivialities of the meeting to those who care about national medicine.

▲ The preparatory committee almost looked forward to piercing the autumn water The meeting was originally scheduled to be held on the 15th, but it was delayed until the 12th. Only a few dozen doctors from various places reported to the meeting. It was thought that the number of people would be difficult to gather at that time, so it was postponed to the 17th. Unexpectedly, between the 13th and 14th, representatives from various places reported one after another, and the number of registered people exceeded 200. The preparatory committee was too busy to entertain them, so they set the 15th to hold a preparatory meeting at Jinling Spring and the 17th to officially hold a meeting at the National Martial Arts Center. I heard that the reason why the initiators from various places were late was mostly due to occupational problems and they could not easily stop seeing patients, so they all set the time to come to Beijing to avoid delays. The preparatory committee did not know this situation and could not help but look forward to it.

▲ National martial arts and national medicine are brothers in distress On that day, many representatives gave speeches, and the speech of a certain gentleman from the National Martial Arts Center was the most interesting. He said that the government ordered the establishment of a National Medical Center, modeled after the National Martial Arts Center. It is a coincidence that the preparatory meeting of the National Medical Center is being held at the National Martial Arts Center. National martial arts can make the weak stronger, and national medicine can make the sick healthy. Different paths lead to the same goal, which can be regarded as brothers in distress. The National Martial Arts Center has been established for three years, but the national medicine is still in the womb. According to the facts, the National Martial Arts Center should be the elder brother. I hope that this little brother will be born as soon as possible so that the brothers can join hands to lead the people to the avenue of health. The metaphor was appropriate and aroused a lot of spirit from the audience.

▲ The lame man left ink marks on his new clothes There was a lame gentleman running around the meeting place quite laboriously. When asked, an acquaintance said that he was He Yunsheng, a representative of the Shanghai Chinese Medicine Association. On that day, Mr. He was wearing a newly made satin robe and was very stylish. Unexpectedly, the chairman accidentally spilled ink on his body and quickly apologized. Mr. He repeatedly said it was okay, and said that he was thinking of leaving a souvenir here today, and this ink stain on his lapel could be called an excellent souvenir. So he limped around, showing his lapel to his friends, and everyone was amused by it.

A Night at the Dance Review 147

— Plum Blossom Hall Master

The Russian Clotilde Sakharoff Dance Troupe has traveled to Europe and the United States, and its reputation has been growing. This time, it was invited to Shanghai by the Xia Ling Pei Ke Theatre. Since March 18th, they have been performing every other day, and every night is sold out, no less than the Tanney Xiang Dance Troupe of the Carlton last year. On the night of the 27th, I went to see the performance with three brothers, Shou Juan, Mu Yun, and Ban Kuang. I was very comfortable in my assigned seat. Although there are only four members in the troupe, the programs are varied and there are many patterns. They are constantly introducing new things, which makes people dazzled. The heroine is Clotilde Sakharoff, and the hero is Aoexa andre Sakharoff. Those who specialize in dancing, on the one hand, have fleshy and sensual breasts and legs, and on the other hand, have bizarre shapes and vivid descriptions. All kinds of dances have special advantages. The Spring Flower Dance and the Black Dance are especially enjoyable for me to watch. The male and female characters are both beautiful in posture and equal in skill. The whole body pays attention to the performance of "power". The waist, chest, hips, abdomen, arms, legs, fingers, and toes all contain powerful elements, so every move can give people a considerable sense of beauty. In addition, Gaveau's piano solo is always in tune, sometimes like a slight wave, leisurely and fascinated, sometimes like a gust of wind and rain, the courage is shocking, the technique is amazing, and the sigh is over. According to my experience, Leitlinger's flamboyance is far beyond the reach of ordinary people's fingers, no wonder the audience's welcome is constant. It is said that the troupe originally planned to leave Shanghai and return to Europe immediately, but due to the sincere retention of the hospital owner, they will continue to perform at the original location on Wednesday night of this week, with new programs added.

— Holding the Moon

It is heard that the sound film "Yu Meiren" produced by Yiming Company and entrusted to Youlian Company has been completely completed. The sound is clear and accurate, the plot is sad and moving, and the grandeur and richness of the scenery are only seen in domestic films. There is a "Fang Cao Mei Ren Song" in the film, which was written by Wu Zhongwen Hao Cheng Zhanlu, and the tune was composed by the famous singer Feng Chunhang, integrating the advantages of Beijing Kunming lyrics into one furnace. Xu Qinfang and Shang Guanwu, the two movie stars, jointly sang it, which is both graceful and majestic. Qian Shiyun praised the beauty of Yu Meiren's lyrics, saying that the silver lights reflect the sad history, and the audience sheds tears together. It is doubtful that it is illusion and truth. It is cast into a big mistake, not without reason. The verdant green grass of the world is endless, where are people like jade? The song of high mountains and flowing water becomes musk, and the setting sun of the double tomb remains for the infatuated soul.

India Travelogue (9) 149

— Linghua

The architecture of Jia City is grand and orderly, much like the Western-style buildings in Shanghai. It's neither very new nor very old. The trees are lush and fresh, resembling Nanjing in its tranquility and Beijing in its stillness. However, the beggars filling the streets are quite unsightly. Although in India, it is difficult for us to distinguish between ascetics and beggars. Indians do not harm birds; birds fly all over the city, and their songs often enter the ear. Indians do not harm birds above, nor cows below; their equality with all creatures is truly admirable. However, if they encounter someone strong enough to subdue them, they are powerless to resist. Even Westerners in India are transformed and do not shoot birds; the law forbids it. Examining this custom, various countries also have some degree of it. Italy forbids harming doves, and Muslims forbid harming spiders, claiming to have saved their religious leader. Now, Indians' kindness extends to birds and beasts, but they cannot defend their own people, which is lamentable. Observing this, one understands the graded love—love for relatives, love for the people, and love for all things—in China, which is the beautiful foundation for creating universal harmony through the nation.

On the 27th, several Ceylon monks came. The Buddhist layperson greeted them with the practice of touching their feet, reminiscent of ancient customs. This so-called head-to-foot greeting. China does not have this custom, but letters still refer to the recipient as "at your feet," which is somewhat close. Now, Buddhism has completely disappeared in the entire central and northern India, only remaining in Ceylon Island and small states in northern Bhutan and Nepal outside of southern India. From there, it connects to Tibet and extends to China. To the east, from Sikkim to Burma, it connects to Siam and reaches China. The relics of Buddhism in Java are also very abundant, and there are now gradual promoters who are Ceylon Buddhists, not Indians. The Indians I have seen, scholars, gentry, and merchants alike, acknowledge the Buddha as one of the Buddhas, respecting but not worshipping him. When asked, they generally say that they are largely the same. I repeatedly asked for their differences, and they all said that the Buddha only talks about cause and effect and does not mention God, while Hinduism talks about God. This is fundamentally different. I briefly examined the differences between Buddhism and Hinduism discussed in the Gedatsu scriptures, and it was indeed so. Atheism is not suitable for the Indian people. However, since the Tang Dynasty, various esoteric masters such as Vajrabodhi and Amoghavajra have all displayed great supernatural powers. Now, Tibetan and Japanese Buddhism both rely on esoteric practices to manifest, so Buddhism cannot be said to be completely devoid of God. Only India and Burma take Theravada as their religion, so they specialize in cultivation and attaining nirvana, self-cause, self-effect, self-nature, and self-salvation. I asked why Ceylon Buddhism is so prosperous. Mr. Xin Han said that according to legend, Buddha once personally preached and transformed in Ceylon. However, Ceylon's written history actually began around 200 BC, coinciding with the Ashoka dynasty. It is credible that King Ashoka sent people to preach everywhere. This is using scientific research. However, Taoist Master Daojie said that Mount Lanka is in Ceylon Island, and the Mahayana Lankavatara Sutra was spoken here, likely through the Buddha's supernatural powers. According to my consideration, it is difficult to examine history based on supernatural powers. Judging from the facts, if one were to travel to Ceylon from the mainland, it would be impossible, but if one were to travel to Ceylon by sea to preach, it would not be difficult. Perhaps the Buddha traveled to Ceylon by sea? However, there is no historical record of the Buddha ever boarding a ship. In the Gospels of Jesus, it is clearly recorded that Jesus rode a boat and a donkey, but Buddhist scriptures do not mention anything. It is difficult to determine.
