Book and Newspaper Introductions

Wild Grass Poetry Special Issue 150

— Nanxin

Volume 4, Number 13

The purely literary Wild Grass Weekly, its content is advancing like the tide, more with each issue. Regardless of the size of a publication, it is important to be grand in quantity to attract readers' attention, but it is also necessary to strive for substance in content. Truly great new literary works in China, possessing the highest artistic value, have not yet been produced in the current state of the Chinese literary scene. This is not to be discouraged. In the current literary publications filled with shoddy works, one can adopt an objective artistic perspective to assess their value itself. On the other hand, readers' appreciation has improved to a certain extent. Those boring works containing low-level tastes and catering to the general public's psychology are unwilling to be read by those who have a slight taste for literature. So-called high-level literature with artistic elements is most welcome by these readers, but this high-level literature mentioned here is rarely seen in the recent Chinese literary scene, or perhaps it can be said that it has not yet been discovered. Even if current publications sometimes publish one or two relatively great works, it is still very weak. What we feel is that the gradual increase in readers' appreciation is indeed a good phenomenon that promotes the advancement of literary works. It cannot be said that the literary works produced by the Chinese literary scene in the future will surpass Western literary works. If we continue to work hard with a faithful artistic attitude to create beautiful and supreme artistic flowers, then Chinese new literature can at least radiate brilliant colors and present more great works to our readers. Perhaps this true meaning of hope can be realized soon.

Secondly, to make the new literature flourish and be of the highest quality and worthy of attention, various publications should adopt strict standards in selecting literary works, while simultaneously making serious and faithful critiques of literary works. These are all paths to promote the advancement of literary works. At present, the general trend of large and small publications selecting literary works has moved towards this path of identifying the essence of literary works, which is a noteworthy and good sign.

The Wild Grass Weekly is thin in quantity, but in reality, it is a publication advancing against the tide of the current literary decline. The content is being innovated with each issue, with a determination to not let the words become empty and powerless. It is indeed striving for the literary movement to have an upward spirit. If it is made into a dull and lifeless publication, it is better not to develop in this literary direction. For the barren literary garden of China, there is no contribution to be made, and it is a waste of effort to irrigate it. After reading Wild Grass, we feel that the organizers are working hard and are a group of faithful literary gardeners, irrigating the barren literary garden with their efforts. The works within, due to space limitations, cannot be accommodated as much as possible in terms of quantity, but in terms of quality, we can clearly see that they are adopting strict standards and rarely engaging in shoddy work. The previously published creation special issue gave us a very good impression and can be considered a contribution to the recent creation world, although the works within cannot be praised as mature and reaching the highest peak of art. Following this, what is being contributed to the literary scene is a poetry special issue. Poetry, according to the current situation, should be promoted to make it shine with brilliant colors in the near future. This is hopeful and realistically possible because the artistic techniques of poetry are gradually becoming sound and mature as readers' appreciation increases. In terms of content, it adopts extraordinary themes, and in terms of form, there is a new expression. This is worth our describing. Compared with the poetic techniques of the "May Fourth" era, there has obviously been a distinctive progress. For example, the poems contained in this issue of the Wild Grass special issue are all on the new path of poetry and are rarely seen in the current Chinese poetry scene.

There are six poems and one prose poem, such as Ms. Yu Shan's "Gratitude," Wang Tiehua's "When the Morning Light Breaks Through the Horizon," Zou Fang's "Peeping into the Tomb from the Grave Gap," Mi Luo's "I Am Waiting for You in the Middle of the Night," Wang Fen's "Ah, the Little Lamb Who Lost His Way," He Fu's "Scraps," Xu Yan's "Yearning in a Dream," Charles's "Remembering a Friend," and Tang Zengyang's "Self-Portrait of a Poet." Each of these poems can represent each author's style, and here we can also see the several forms contained in poetry and the new path that poetry should take in the future.

The first one worth mentioning is indeed Ms. Yu Shan's "Gratitude." This female poet seems to be making her debut on Wild Grass, but her poetry is already so mature and gratifying that we should praise her. The passionate abandon is truly like that expressed by Byron. The bold description surpasses the maternal love depicted by the female poet Bing Xin. The structure of the poem is exceptionally mature, the meaning is profound, the wording is appropriate, and the rhetoric is refined, all of which are rarely seen in recent poetry. There are two sections in which I think the most sincere expressions are revealed, which are quoted below for readers to appreciate:

You must deeply understand the heart of the poet,

Like trying to grasp a swirling fish in the depths of the abyss.

It once burned like a volcanic eruption—for you,

It once flowed like a Yellow River breach—for you.

I want to love you, I want to cherish you,

But alas, I fear that you lack courage, my friend,

And will waste my true feelings and sincere intentions.

You love me—love my beautiful appearance,

You cherish me—cherish my youth,

How can I love you, how can I be foolish for you?

The unsound will is drifting wildly in the wind.

Who can keep youth for long in this drizzly dusk?

Such a passion filled with love is carved out with sincere poetic strokes, especially coming from the heart of a girl, it is worthy of our praise and admiration. It is not easy to see such a mature artistic technique. Almost all of Yu's poems are tense and powerful. Finally, her use of repeated sentences to construct the structure shows that the author is moving towards a new path in poetry and not sinking into the vortex of vulgarity, which can be compared with the old techniques. This is also the unique characteristic of this poem. At the same time, the author's consciousness is upward. In this poem, there is no trace of the so-called sadness of the poet.

Wang Tiehua's "When the Morning Light Breaks Through the Horizon" is a heroic nationalist poem. In form, it is extremely oriented towards a new path that has not been expressed by any poet. In other words, it is a poem with a new style and new techniques. From this, we can also see the technological progress of nationalist poetry.

When the morning light breaks through the horizon,

The dewdrops redden our toes.

We roar in unison, watching the clouds fly in disarray.

Ah, the tragic and magnificent rivers and mountains will forever mark a glorious battle.

Beautiful poetic realm, ah, why have you forgotten to wander and sing?

The splashing of blood flowers, ah, how can it match the heroic poetic soul?

Tighten your fiery rhythm,

Seek the life of the nation, not refusing our death.

This novel expression and heroic spirit show that nationalist poetry is trending towards the peak of art and is greater than other general poems, which is worthy of our attention.

Zou Fang's poem also represents a style and is also a powerful work.

He Fu's "Scraps" is a poem with neat sentences that was once popular in the Chinese poetry scene. Charles's "Remembering a Friend" is a prototype of poetry in the May Fourth era and is worthy of our attention. Tang Zengyang's "Self-Portrait of a Poet" is a beautiful prose poem. The poems of Wang Fen, Xu Yan, and Mi Luo are also worth reading.

This issue of the poetry special issue has extremely rich content. We can see various new poetic forms and at the same time, it can indicate to us clearly the new path that new poetry should take. This is extremely praiseworthy.

Manuscript Guidelines for Book and Newspaper Introductions 153

(1) Literature is limited to introducing the latest publications at home and abroad. In addition to literary works, all political, economic, legal, scientific, and other books and newspapers are included in the introduction. However, trivial books and newspapers are not introduced.

(2) Pictures are limited to the latest works of new writers at home and abroad and illustrations related to the text.

(3) Articles on textual research or research on ancient Chinese books will not be published.

(4) Pictures and photos are limited to those related to the text.

(5) Each article should not exceed 3,000 words.

(6) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(7) Do not draw pictures with blue ink and do not use colored paper. Use white paper and black ink.

(8) Please indicate "Book and Newspaper Introduction Editor Receives" on the manuscript.

(9) Submitted manuscripts will not be returned regardless of whether they are published or not. If a return is required, please state this in advance and attach sufficient postage.

(10) Compensation for text is divided into three levels: three yuan, two yuan, and one yuan per thousand words. The same applies to pictures and photos. If there are special manuscripts, the compensation will be calculated separately.

(11) Compensation for text is divided into three levels: three yuan, two yuan, and one yuan per thousand words. The compensation for each picture and photo is the same. If there are special manuscripts, the compensation will be calculated separately.

Youth Garden

Miscellaneous Records of a Trip to the North 154

— Anping

4. "My Gemma"

I got up on the 2nd morning, ate something, and after taking care of my train ticket at the China Travel Agency in Xiaguan, we planned to go to Zhongshan Mausoleum to pay respects to the tomb.

The main reason I was willing to stay in Nanjing this time was to pay my respects to Zhongshan Mausoleum. I still remember when I last left Nanjing in the year of the May 30th Massacre, I thought it wouldn't be too difficult to come to Nanjing again. However, the ups and downs of life pass by in an instant, and it's been a full six years. If I didn't stop in Nanjing this time, who could say when I would come to Nanjing again? So I didn't want to abandon this "convenience."

They all agreed when they heard that I wanted to go to Zhongshan Mausoleum, except that Hao couldn't ask for leave, so he didn't go.

After lunch, it was already one o'clock. We walked together to Shenmiao Kou to hire a car. The driver seemed to want three and a half yuan, and we bargained it down to two yuan.

I suddenly wanted to ride a horse, and Xi and Hongzhu were also willing. I asked them if they had ever ridden, and they both said no. I said that I had never ridden a horse either. So everyone revealed a bit of hesitation, but young people have courage, curiosity, and a fresh and lively spirit. It doesn't matter if no one knows how to ride, as long as they are happy and not forced.

However, horses are too expensive, two yuan per hour. Going to Zhongshan Mausoleum and back wouldn't be enough in three hours, so wouldn't it cost more than twenty yuan for the three of us? It seemed like the price was too high to ride, but I didn't want to give up in my heart. At that time, the desire to ride a horse was so strong that even if the driver was willing to hire a car to us for two yuan, I wouldn't want it. However, the price difference was too great, and it seemed like there was no hope. But Tian Tian actually helped out. Helped with what? Don't worry, I'll tell you.

It turned out that because we wanted to hire horses, somehow there was a misunderstanding, and two horse dealers started arguing with each other. Fortunately, due to the argument, one of them was willing to rent three horses to us at the price of one yuan per hour.

None of the three of us had ever ridden a horse, and none of us had any knowledge about riding. Everyone thought, "I don't want to go first, and I don't want to go last. It's best to be in the middle."

In the end, I still went first. Although I hadn't been to Nanjing for six or seven years, I was naturally more familiar with the route than they were. After passing Fuqiao and Daxinggong, I couldn't help but feel a little timid. Once I got on Zhongshan Avenue, I seemed to have gained courage. After the horse whip made a very graceful gesture in the air, it flashed like lightning across the horse's rear. With a most agile and nimble step, the white horse with a body covered in snow-like patches began to gallop. Like an extremely skilled rider, I held the reins with one hand and pinched the whip with the other, keeping my body steady with the most appropriate center of gravity and the most graceful posture. Whistling in my mouth, the companions on both sides only saw the scenery receding behind us. The wind gently brushed my face, without a trace of coolness. A healthy, lively, and youthful feeling passed through my veins like electricity.

The journey of more than twenty li seemed to take less than forty minutes. A mausoleum of such grandeur appeared before my eyes. I got off the horse, led it to an open space, and tied it up, waiting for Xi and Hongzhu to arrive together before going up. But after waiting for more than twenty minutes, I still didn't see them. I really couldn't have this patience anymore.

With an extremely solemn heart and slow steps, I walked up. Walking on the stone steps, I often turned back to look at the mountain trees like a painting, the white and shallow Zhongshan Road, the black circle of the city wall, and the black dots inside the city wall. "What a magnificent atmosphere!" I realized in my heart as I walked into the Li Gate to sign my name. With the most honorable, proud, and solemn attitude, I wrote these three words on the signature book:

"Chu Anping"

I wandered around the mausoleum for a long time, my heart as still as if it had died. Solemnity occupied my entire consciousness. I really wanted to sit on the stone steps and think aimlessly.

They didn't come until then. Xi often wanted to talk to me, but I didn't want him to disturb my peaceful mood and said, "Please forgive me, let's talk about everything later."

At the foot of the mausoleum, there were many white cloth sheds, like a summer camp of Boy Scouts. They were all selling tea and coffee. We had three cups of cocoa.

At that time, the summit of Zijin Mountain was already covered in a haze. It was going to rain, so we had to quickly get on our horses and hurry back to the city. We didn't even have time to go to Linggu Temple.

Returning on horseback was more skilled and experienced than when we came. Fortunately, the rain didn't come down heavily, just a drizzle. However, this drizzle was better than nothing. You think, riding on horseback, the mood is so smooth and pleasant. Coming back with a little drizzle is really like being a god.

After returning to school, Xi said many complimentary things to me. These words came from the bottom of his heart, but he was truly someone who liked to exaggerate when he spoke. However, I, who usually didn't really want to get his praise, was overjoyed when he said this sentence to me:

Page 22

He said, "When I saw you riding a horse, your posture was so graceful and handsome and natural that I unconsciously associated you with Sanin in Turgenev's Spring Torrents."

Thank you for this sentence. Although it startled me when I heard it, I was indeed happy. Not only happy, but also grateful for his seriousness.

Alas, Sanin, how can I have a beautiful figure like Sanin, a good-looking face, a pair of light blue eyes, a gentle expression, all yellow hair, delicate red and white skin, the most endearing special, natural, pleasant, sincere, and frank expression, a childlike smile, innocent, healthy, gentle, gentle, gentle... Alas, Sanin, how can I compare to such a Sanin as written by Turgenev?

However, honest nephew Xi was really saying it so solemnly that he unconsciously associated it with me when he saw me riding a horse.

Yes, if I were Sanin, if I were someone called Dmitry Pavlovich Sanin, then I would beg God not to let me meet such a woman as Maria Nikolaevna Polozova. If I really met her, then with her thick and beautiful hair, her lovely neck, her beautiful shoulders, her slender figure, her intoxicating and charming gesture that makes people go crazy at first sight, and that woman walking towards a person as if she has brought all the happiness of a person's life to meet him, her soft voice, her long, red, moist lips, the dimples when she smiles, that intimate and seemingly soft voice... and as Pushkin said, whoever meets her will stand still and be fascinated by her, but she is not standing before "the shrine of beauty," but under the magic of a half-Russian, half-Gypsy woman with blooming flowers and flourishing magic, making people stand still and be fascinated by her and never feel reluctant ... and I, I would rather stay with my Gemma and kneel at her feet, pressing my face against her waist and saying:

"My Gemma, rest assured, I will always be yours."

Home
